“Losers cook dinner.” Wanda suggested. The other teammates were currently out getting groceries for the weekend. 

“You’re on. Let’s play first to 11 wins.” Horsey agreed and laid the ground rules. 

Peggy took the first serve and shot it over the net. Agatha got the first bump, Lupe bumped it again back over. Flo passed it up in the air, Horsey set it, and Rio ran up and delivered a cracking spike. First point. 

“Are you a secret pro volleyball player too?” Agatha jeered. 

“I like all sports. Not my fault, I tend to be good at most of them.” Rio responded as her teammates all came over to give her high-fives. 

Horsey’s team went ahead quickly 5-1, as Rio continued to wallop her impressive spikes on the unprepared defense. Agatha was able to block a few, but it was no use. Wanda was able to put a few more points on their tally, but they were outmatched. 

On the matchpoint, Agatha served. She watched as the ball bounced between Peggy then Flo. She saw Rio sizing up the ball, tracking it through the air, her eyes locked on their target. The pitcher took a few steps forward and launched into the air, her arm rising above her head and connecting with the ball perfectly. It fired down and hit the ground despite Agatha’s attempt at it. 

Game over. 

“What a game, Rio! If you ever leave baseball, you should see if any volleyball teams will take you.” Dottie patted her on the back and grabbed a soda from the cooler. 

Wanda took the lead on cooking. She was easily the most competent cook in the house, although they were just having a weenie roast. She made her mom’s Sokovian potato salad, a delicious, Eastern European-inspired side dish. Lupe manned the post at the grill and casually turned the ears of corn and hot dogs over the coals. 

Agatha avoided all responsibility and sat down on one of the lawn chairs around the fire pit. The sun was very slowly setting, and Horsey was attempting to start the fire. Rio and Buckets were kicking around a soccer ball with the twins.

“This is quite a place, Horsey. You’re lucky to have a spot like this in your family.” Agatha said. 

“Thanks, Angel. It’s pretty great, huh? Your family doesn’t have a vacation spot?”

Agatha let out a sharp laugh, “I never left my state until I went to Chicago for try-outs. My mom wasn’t into traveling, vacationing, or the concept of fun.”

Wanda came down from the kitchen, arms full of food. She dumped it onto the serving table with the rest of the dishes and drinks. “Food’s ready, come and get it!” 

Agatha grabbed a paper plate and loaded it up with everything in sight - a scoop of potato salad, a scoop of coleslaw, a bread roll, corn on the cob, a slice of watermelon, and two hot dogs. She poured a glass of lemonade and carefully sat back near the fire. 

The twins carried their plates and sat in the grass behind the firepit. Wanda brought over a blanket and joined them on the ground. Peggy sat beside them, and Rio took up the spot next to Agatha. 

“Thanks for this amazing meal, Wanda.” She turned around and gave her compliments to the chef. 

“You’re welcome, Rio. It was no trouble. I love cooking.” 

“Why?” Agatha groaned. 

“Some of us can’t go out to eat for every meal or have host families that cook for us daily.” Wanda said. 

“What can I say? I’m blessed in many ways.” Agatha lifted her corn cob and munched away at the kernels. 

“Auntie Aggie, watch me.” Billy waited for her to turn and watch as he copied her and devoured his corn cob like a beaver going after a log. 

“Nice work, kiddo. Don’t choke.” She said back. 

“So, Rio…we don’t know much about you. Do you got a fella back home?” Dottie looked over the pitcher. 

Rio finished swallowing a bite of hot dog and took a drink of her Coke, “Nope. No boyfriend for me. I’ve actually never dated any fella.”

Agatha gasped along with several of the others, “Never?!”

Rio smirked over at her, “Is that so surprising?” 

“It’s just…you’re so…I mean, surely you had guys asking you out at school?” She struggled to articulate her point. 

“Sure, plenty asked, but you know that you can say no, right?”

“So you’ve never even kissed anyone?” Peggy asked like it was the most outrageous thought. 

“I never said that.” Rio grinned like a Cheshire cat to the “oohs” and “ahhs” of the group. She locked eyes with Agatha, and the catcher felt a sudden heat spark between them. Agatha averted her eyes, feeling suddenly embarrassed like she was caught doing something she shouldn’t. 

“Okay, let’s go around and say the worst kiss you’ve ever had.” Peggy clapped her hands and rubbed them together slyly. 

“I’ll go!” Helen pulled her chair over from the picnic table. “A few years ago, I went on a first date with the gym teacher. He took me to the cinema, which was fine, and then drove me home. He was so nervous, it was almost endearing, but then he went in for a kiss, and I could see the sweat dripping across his upper lip. I couldn’t do it. I ran from that car and had to avoid him for the rest of the school year.”

Everyone cracked up around the circle. 

“I got one.” Dottie volunteered. “I was in my last year of high school. This boy, Richie, asked me to the dance. He was a tall drink of iced tea if I ever saw one, so of course, I said yes. Richie was a real jive bomber on the dance floor and could move his hips. We were the center of attention that night. A slow number came on, and he started pulling me close. My arms were around his neck, his hands were on my waist. 

He was looking at my lips. He leaned in, and I swear he opened his mouth as big as a bullfrog. He was fixin’ to swallow me, and his lips completely covered mine in a wet, sloppy mess. It was awful. I pushed him away after a few seconds of painful endurance and said I had to powder my nose. I made sure to get off the dance floor any time another slow song was played!”

“God, I hate when they open their mouths like that! It’s disgusting. I don’t want to see what you had for breakfast!” Peggy added. 

“Who told them that we like that? Did we miss some telegram or something?” Helen asked. 

“What about when they use their tongue like a weapon?” Lupe began fake gagging at the thought. 

Peggy jumped in next, “My worst kiss is easy. Well, my worst almost-kiss. It was the off season, and I’d just finished my first year with the league. I went back to Salem with Agatha, and we went out on the town in Boston and a group of G.I.s were at this bar. One soldier with platinum blonde hair buys me a drink. He starts talking about how he’s shipping out soon, how he wishes he could spend one more night with a lady before he goes, blah blah blah. I’d heard it all before, and he’d had more than a few drinks; he was getting proper pissed. 

I let him buy me a few more and chat me up. He was handsome, but he pulled me out to the alleyway and pinned me up against the wall. It was not entirely unpleasant, but then as he went in for the kiss, I closed my eyes, and then felt something warm dripping down my back as I heard him retch over my shoulder. He vomited all over the wall behind me. I couldn’t even speak. I just left him there and went to get Agatha and go.”

“Oh, the smell in the taxi home. I can still remember it viscerally.” Agatha groaned. 

“Y’all really know how to turn a girl’s stomach. I’m going to head to bed!” Dottie stood up, along with a few others who grabbed their plates and went up to the house. Now that the sun was gone, it was a whole different kind of dark. Given the isolation of the place, it was tough to see right in front of you. 

Agatha helped Wanda carry the rest of the dishes up to the kitchen, and Rio helped Horsey put out the fire and clean the grill. Wanda went to put the boys to bed as they were already up way past their usual bedtime, and when Agatha finished washing up, she took the stairs down to the lower floor. 

Rio still wasn’t back yet, so she decided to take a shower in the bathroom and get changed into her pajamas, a sleeveless polka-dot top with matching wide-leg bottoms. She unrolled her sleeping bag onto the firmest of the three couches and grabbed two of the pillows. Then, she pulled the heavy curtains across the row of windows, leaving just a small opening to let in the sun in the morning. 

She scanned the books on the many shelves and tried to find anything decent to read, but it seemed like everything was an old mystery or a penny drama. As she was about to give up hope, Rio slid open the glass door.

Chapter 12: Warming up

Every season, from spring training in April until September, the women of the All-American Girls Baseball League played eight games per week—six nights and Sunday doubleheaders. Only the weather would grant the occasional day off. “Believe me, we prayed for rain,” remembered pitcher Dorothy “Dottie” Wiltse.

“You think people call me Buckets at home?” Loretta laughed. She had been given the moniker after her last name “Buckley.” 

“We should give her a name to strike fear into the hearts of the batters. Something menacing or scary.” Dottie suggested. 

“Rocket? Because of her speed?” Wanda threw it out there. 

“Hmmm, Vixen Vidal?” Betty asked. 

“No, we need something intimidating.” Peggy shook her head. 

“What about the Raven? They’re often the symbol of ill fortune.” Horsey offered. 

“Rio the Raven. That has a certain something to it.” Peggy said, looking towards the pitcher in question who bobbed her head side to side indecisively. 

“The Reaper.” Agatha declared boldly, and the room was abuzz instantly with sounds of affirmation. 

“Ooooh, Rio “The Reaper” Vidal. Now that’s a nickname. She’s here to take the soul of every batter who dares challenge her. She’s all-knowing, she’s ruthless, she’s inevitable.” Peggy loved the name immediately. 

Rio was smiling widely, “I like it.” It felt like she was in, like she was part of the club now. 

The game started with a bang as the Comets went up by one run in the very first inning. Rio gave up two hits as the Peaches fought back, but the defence was able to hold them and prevent anyone from scoring. 

Agatha was up in the second inning and scorched a line drive right above the pitcher for a base hit. Fern advanced her to second base, but the next two batters went down on easy plays to first. Dottie struck out swinging on a close fastball, and the side was retired. 

“Rio, this next group of batters is the best on their team. Let’s up the tempo and keep them guessing, alright?” Agatha counselled the pitcher as they took the field for the bottom of the second inning. 

“I trust you.” Rio acknowledged and took to the mound. The crowd was loud as over 5,000 fans packed the stands. The Rockford fans were notoriously loyal and fervent supporters of their ball club. 

Rio let the noise wash over her and quieted her mind. She closed her eyes and rolled her throwing arm to shake it loose. When she opened her eyes again, they immediately snapped to the shining blues behind the catcher’s mask.

Agatha watched Mary Richards come up to bat. Richie, as she was often called, was a jumpy hitter. She swung outside the zone at a higher than average percentage, but she was also more likely to get on base because of her risky swings. Agatha threw down a two for a curveball. 

Rio accepted the sign and started her wind-up. Agatha watched the ball leave the pitcher’s hand and saw the deceptive arc as it started high and dropped down low. Mary swung as if she expected it to hit dead center and was shocked when she missed it completely for a strike. 

The next fastball hit Agatha’s glove hard, and the batter watched it zoom past for strike two. Rio closed it out with a third heater in the bottom inside corner. 

“Wow.” Mary breathed out as she made the walk of shame back to the home team dugout. 

That word would be muttered several more times as Rio continued to dominate the next four innings, striking out another five batters. 

“Let’s go Reaper, let’s go Reaper.” The Comets players shouted and clapped from their bench to cheer on their star pitcher. Even some fans started to join the chants. 

When Bobbie Key came up to the plate, Agatha knew this would be the perfect test for Rio’s knuckleball. Bobbie had a great batting average and knew her stuff. She wasn’t often fooled but sometimes struggled with slower pitches. When she took her stance, Agatha called for the knuckleball right out of the gate. She knew Bobbie would be expecting a fastball. Rio almost always started with it, and it was her most dominant pitch. 

The pitcher gave Agatha a subtle smile as she adjusted her grip on the ball. Her wind-up mirrored her normal delivery but when she released, the baseball had almost no spin on it at all. It looked like it was floating right towards the plate. Bobbie swung early anticipating the speed and watched with pain as the ball dropped into the glove after she’d already gotten the bat over the plate. Strike. 

Wow. This time it was Agatha who was impressed. 

The Peaches tied it up in the seventh at 1-1, but the Comets got their bats going in the final inning and went ahead 4-1 for the win. Rio was relieved from the game in the eighth by Betty, but she still got the win on her record for her performance that game. 

“Another solid win, Comets.” Coach Grant spoke to them in the dugout as they were packing up. “Let’s keep this up and sail through August. The playoffs are waiting for us!”

Chapter 13: Take me out to the ball game

“Love the game of baseball and baseball will love you.” Babe Ruth

“Nice job against those Peaches, girls. Just one loss isn’t too bad, right?” Gertie asked Peggy and Agatha over dinner on their first night back home.

“Not bad? It’s pretty damn good, I’d say.” Peggy replied in good spirits. 

“How many games do you have left?” Pearl asked. 

“16 games until the playoffs start in September. We are guaranteed to make it at this point. It’s just a matter of positioning. First place gets the best match-up against the fourth place team, while second and third have to go against each other. Then, the winner of those games battles it out in the finals for the championship.” Agatha explained. 

“What other teams do you think will make it?” Gertie questioned as she cut her chicken with a knife and fork. 

“The Blue Sox and us for sure. And then it’s a race between the Chicks, the Belles, and the Peaches. The Lassies have a pathway, but it’s so unlikely that I don’t see it happening.” Agatha tracked the team positioning very closely after every game. She liked to know her competition inside and out. 

“Whatever happened to those orphan teams? The ones that had to shut down.” Pearl wondered. 

“Last I heard they were going on the road. I think the managers set up exhibition games all across the east coast and the south. They are trying to spark interest across the country. It’s to make money, but I think they are desperate for more talent. The pool of female ball players is shrinking fast.” Peggy said. They had heard from Coach Grant about the plans for the Sallies and the Colleens not long after Rio had joined them. 

“Well they need to get more organizations to start baseball leagues for the kiddos. If every young lady is stuck playing softball, there aren’t going to be many baseball stars to pick from in a few years.” Gertie said. 

Agatha nodded in agreement, “That’s the sad truth. I just hope they let us finish this year out at least. Whatever happens next is up to those that make so much more money than me. The crowds have been bigger than ever, but we’re losing all the top girls to marriage, babies, or more stable careers.” 

“Who are you playing next?” Pearl asked. 

“We’ve got the Lassies at home. They’re on a winning streak, but I don’t think they will be a problem. We’ve crushed them at every series over the past few years.” Peggy said. 

That prediction was spot on. The Comets sent the Lassies packing with four straight wins in a row. Agatha bagged her 19th homer of the season. Rio racked up another win as a starting pitcher. Peggy was on a nine-game hitting streak, and even Wanda was setting personal records with her 30th RBI when she sent Dottie home on a double. 

After their impressive series sweep, Coach Grant brought up a proposition at their afternoon practice the next day, “As many of you know, I played in the majors a few years ago.”

The team members side-eyed each other and all let out a friendly collective groan. 

“Yeah, yeah. You might not be groaning once you hear this.” He gestured his hands like he was pushing down to try to quiet the chatter. “My old teammate, “Big Bear” Garcia pitches for the Cleveland Indians, and he said he could get me four tickets for their upcoming game against the White Sox in Chicago. The game is already sold out so that’s as many as he could get.”

Everyone started whispering in excitement at the prospect of getting to see a major league game in person. “Well? Who gets to go?” Agatha was the first to pipe up. 

Coach smiled, “You all deserve it, so I figure the only fair way to do this is…a batting contest. Ten hits. 100 points for a homer, 50 points for outfield, 25 for infield, and 0 for foul balls or strikes. Top three batters get the tickets.” 

“I thought you said there were four tickets?” Peggy looked at him with her eyes narrowed. 

“Yeah, one’s for me, of course.” He admitted without shame. He was also a huge baseball fan and always enjoyed catching a game. The team showered him with “boos” that he welcomed. 

“If I pitch for this, can I still be a batter?” Rio asked. 

“Everyone can put their hat in. Can you pitch back-up, Lupe?” Coach looked at the other starting pitching who nodded. “Alright, you guys ready? Let’s do it!” 

They sat in the dugout in batting order as Rio warmed up with Agatha. 

“Nice and easy. Keep it to fastballs but take some heat off them.” The catcher called out as they got ready for the contest. 

“Got it, boss.” Rio replied with a smile. 

Coach Grant stood in the third base coach’s box, “Dottie, you’re first!” 

The southern belle stretched her neck as she walked out to the box, “Don’t kill my dreams, Reaper!” She yelled out to the pitcher. 

Rio tossed the pitches right over the plate. Dottie got four into the outfield (one hit off the fence just a few inches off a home run), three infield hits, and three foul balls. 275 points. 

Wanda put up an impressive 350, and Horsey got angry after only racking up 200. 

“Watch and learn, ladies!” Peggy strolled to the box using her bat as a cane. She got a chip off two good pitches which fell into the infield for 50 points, but then knocked a long ball out past the fences for the full hundred. After ten, her score sat at the top of the table with 425. 

Shirley got unlucky with three foul balls, which dropped her down to 225. Then it was Agatha’s turn. Helen swapped out as catcher as she went to grab her favorite bat. 

“Put ‘em here, Rio!” Agatha extended her bat across the plate, showing the pitcher where she wanted to swing. Rio gave her a conciliatory nod.  

The first ball came right on target and Agatha transferred all her power through her hips to send the ball soaring to the farthest part of center field for a home-run. She beamed as Rio turned and watched the ball fall over the fence. 

Five more dotted the outfield and two more went yard. One should have been a homer but it took an arcing curve and landed just foul for a disappointing zero points. As Agatha’s strength waned, the final pitch popped straight up into the infield, but she knocked Peggy down to take the number one spot with 575. 

“That’s what I’m talking about! Great work, Angel.” Coach Grant applauded her performance. 

Fern, Edna, and Buckets put up solid scores but didn’t crack the top three. Flo managed to take third as she pushed Wanda down with a score of 375. Sugar tied Dottie’s score, and then Helen broke 300 but it still wasn’t enough. Lupe managed to get a homer but couldn’t repeat her success and finished with 325. 

The young substitute, Betty, approached with a fierce determination in her eyes. 

“Let’s go batter! Hit it out of here, Betty!” The team cheered on the rookie. 

To everyone’s surprise, she connected on the first pitch and launched the ball clear of the fences by several feet. Even Betty’s jaw dropped at the sight, she had never hit a homer before. The onlookers jumped and cheered at the impressive sight. She continued launching them into the outfield and connected with a few grounders to take the third spot from Flo with a total of 400 even. 

There was only one batter left. Lupe took the mound as Rio jogged over to get her bat. She just needed to beat Betty’s score to get a ticket. 

Agatha pushed her mask up as Rio came closer, “Hey, don’t worry, I’ll give you a play-by-play of the game if you don’t earn a ticket.” 

Rio scoffed and kicked her feet into place in the dirt, “Don’t get your hopes up, babe.” 

Lupe fired in the first pitch and Rio swung hard and missed. 

“Ooh, do you want the pitcher to slow it down for you?” Agatha heckled her from her crouching position, enjoying the opportunity to get under her skin for once. 

Rio did not respond. Instead, she took her blasé stance again as Lupe wound up. The crack off the bat echoed in Agatha’s ears as the ball flew high and deep towards left field. Rio turned her head and smirked while the catcher could only watch the home-run hit the grass. 

“Nothing more to say?” Rio asked without looking back as she awaited the next pitch. Agatha grizzled but couldn’t respond. 

The talented pitcher knocked four into the outfield, two more over the fence, and one grounder on a high fastball. Her final pitch was headed for right field but dropped just before the grass so only counted for a quarter. She was just barely off Agatha’s total and managed to steal second with 550. 

“Almost had me.” Agatha pushed Rio gently with her catcher’s mitt as they walked together towards the team. 

“I should have let that high one go by.” Rio shook her head regretting that one pitch. 

“Better luck next time.” Agatha replied. 

Coach Grant stood in front of the lined up team and pulled the tickets out of his pocket, “Maybe I should incentivize you more - that was the best hitting I’ve seen in practice since I started coaching you gals! Come up and get your prize, Agatha, Rio, and Peggy!” 

The three winners each took a ticket and waved it in their hand with glee. 

“Meet me here on the 17th, and I’ll drive us to the game. Congratulations again.” He said to them, “Everyone else, I’ll see you tomorrow for our first game against the Daisies.”

They had a doubleheader against Fort Wayne to start off the series and each team took one win. The Daisies had no path to the playoffs but the team still played with all the heart and toughness of a group that hated to lose. They didn’t make it easy, but the Comets pulled off two more wins at home and watched their dreams come clearer and clearer into focus. 

On August 17th, Peggy and Agatha walked together to the ballpark to meet the Coach for their big day out. Peggy looked sharp in a navy blue dress with a high neckline and contrasting red bands highlighting her waist. Agatha, meanwhile, opted for a two-piece peplum top dress in burgundy - the belt, side draping, and stiff shoulders gave her an alluring hourglass shape. 

Their hair was elegantly styled in brushed out waves as they made their way along the sidewalk, their low heels clicking with each step. 

“Do you think it’ll be a close game?” Peggy asked. Agatha followed the Red Sox closely, so she had a general knowledge on the standings in the American League. 

“Have you seen the White Sox record this season? They are hopeless! Cleveland is currently in second behind Boston, who are leading the division, but they are looking really strong.” Agatha explained. 

“Hey, there’s Rio!” Peggy pointed across the street as their teammate approached from the other direction. Agatha stared at the pitcher who looked cool and casual in a white collared, short sleeve blouse paired with a tartan pleated skirt in brown and green. She had on a pair of slingbacks and a fancy beret. 

Rio whistled low when she caught sight of the pair of them, “I fear I’ve underdressed now that I’ve seen you two beauties.” 

“Oh hush, you look amazing, hun.” Agatha greeted her with a swift hug as Peggy did the same. 

Coach Grant pulled up in his Chevrolet Fleetmaster, the one splurge he let himself have these past few years. It was strange seeing him outside his baseball uniform. He was wearing a well-loved light tan suit with white shirt and red tie. 

“I’m one lucky fella to be able to take you three beautiful women out on my own!” He exclaimed as he stepped out and opened the passenger doors for them. 

“Thanks Coach.” Peggy said as she stepped into the front seat. 

“Call me Doc while we’re off the field, please.” His real name was Victor, but he’d earned the nickname Doc in the minor leagues due to his skill at saving a team on the brink of a loss with his home base plays as catcher. 

Rio and Agatha were once again together, this time in the backseat for the hour-long journey to Chicago. They were off to Comiskey Park, near the south side of the city. 

“Have you ever been to a major league game, Rio?” Peggy turned and asked as the car pulled onto the road. 

Rio shook her head, “Nope, only in my dreams. I grew up listening to games on the radio, but there are no teams south of Kentucky and definitely not all the way down in Florida, so I’ve never had a chance.”

“I’ve only been twice. Peggy and I saw the Cubs play our first year in the league when Mr. Wrigley offered tickets to all the girls who made the rosters. And then, we went to see the Red Sox play in Boston last October after our season ended. It’s amazing, you’re gonna love it.” Agatha said. 

When they finally arrived and walked up to the gates, the entire area was swarmed with fans. There were tens of thousands of people vying to either get tickets or get inside. Rio grabbed Agatha’s hand to avoid getting lost in the crowd, and she enjoyed the feeling of security as they slowly made their way to the ticket takers. She tried not to read into the innocent gesture but loved the feeling of connection. Agatha didn’t release her hand until they were all the way to their seats.  

The seats were good as they navigated to the third base side and took their spots about twenty rows back from the field. 

“Wow, how many people does this place hold?” Rio asked as she looked around at the packed stands that surrounded the entire diamond. 

“They say 50,000.” Doc leaned over and said. It was an unfathomable amount of people. Their games typically topped out at around 5,000 (if they were lucky). 

As game time approached, they heard the announcer come over the booming speakers, “Ladies and gentleman, as you may have heard this morning on the wire, our sport and our world has lost a giant. Babe Ruth passed away last night in his sleep at the age of 53. He changed baseball forever and will never be forgotten. We ask you all to stand now as we observe a moment of silence for this titan of the game.” 

Agatha and her teammates looked at each other in complete and utter shock. They hadn’t read the paper this morning or listened to the radio, so they hadn’t heard this devastating news. Tears fell from Doc’s eyes as the reality hit him that Babe Ruth was really gone. Even Agatha’s eyes began to well up. It seemed unbelievable. How could baseball go on without him?

He was one of the few star pitchers who was also a power slugger. Known as the Sultan of Swat or the Great Bambino, Ruth was the greatest baseball player to ever live. As they all stood and felt the collective silence of fifty thousand stunned fans grappling with the loss, Rio took Agatha’s hand again and stroked it gently with her thumb as a show of comfort and a sign of support. She felt the catcher gently squeeze her hand as the moment passed. 

“Now, we’ll hear the national anthem performed by the Chicago Chamber Choir.” The announcer stated as a large group of singers walked out onto the field. The crowd remained standing for the anthem, which was immediately followed by “Play ball!”

“I can’t believe Babe Ruth is gone. I never thought it would happen.” Peggy said as they sat back down. 

“Tell me about it. He wasn’t an old man either. He retired before I was called up, but he’s not much older than me.” Doc said, looking shell-shocked. 

The White Sox took to the field, and Bill Wight was the starting pitcher. The fans favored the home team, but there was a very sizable mix of Cleveland fans throughout the stands given the close proximity of the teams. 

The first two batters grounded out and the third hit a long fly ball to right field that was snagged for an easy inning. Then, the Indians were on the field. 

“Rio, check this out!” Doc nudged her as the new pitcher slowly walked out from the dugout to a blend of cheers and boos. “He just signed with the Indians this year. One of the greatest pitchers in the Negro Leagues, Satchel Paige.”

They watched the incredibly tall Black man take the mound and Rio leaned forward in interest, “No way! I’ve heard of him. He played for the Guayama Witch Doctors in the Puerto Rican League! My Uncle used to talk about him all the time. I think he still holds the strikeout record on the island.” 

“No kidding, I saw him when he played with the Kansas City Monarchs. Just watch his technique. He’s 42! I worried if he would still have the juice, but he’s on another level. His catalog of pitches is crazy. Watch for his eephus pitch, it’s a high curve, or his tailing fastball.” 

Major League Baseball had only integrated the year prior, 1947, when the Brooklyn Dodgers signed Jackie Robinson as a first baseman. Satchel Paige was the 7th Black player so far in the league. He was also the oldest debutant in league history. 

Rio watched enraptured as Paige started his windup. He leaned back then leaned forward and separated his arms and threw them back behind him before bringing them together up on top of his cap, lifting his knee up and striding forward while releasing the ball. It was a hypnotic rhythmic ritual that seemed like second nature to him. 

Agatha watched Rio watching the talented pitcher. Her eyes were locked on his every movement. Agatha saw her mouth open slightly in awe as a blazing strike was called by the ump, and she watched the frustration break across Rio’s brow when a close pitch was deemed a ball. 

“The game’s over there.” Peggy elbowed her softly and pointed towards the field with a smile. Agatha clicked her tongue to stop herself biting back at her nosy friend. 

It was a close contest as both pitchers and their defenses held the score at 0-0. It wasn’t until the bottom of the fourth inning that the Indians got two men on base and center fielder Larry Doby batted in the lead runner to put them ahead 1-0. 

The sound of the crowd was almost deafening as the White Sox fans tried to rally their team. Unfortunately for them, this Cleveland group was incredibly strong. Satchel Paige never faced more than four batters each inning as he struck out several of his opponents and the defense handled any ball hit their way. Both pitchers lasted the full nine innings, and when the game finished Paige was credited with a shutout as the Chicago side failed to score a run against him. 

“That was amazing!” Rio raved as they made their way out of the ballpark. “I’ve never seen pitching like that in all my life.” 

“I hope it’s inspired you. Pitching continues to evolve thanks to all this talent in the majors, so there is always more to learn.” Coach said. 

“Definitely. I can’t wait to try out some of those moves from Satchel Paige. I wish I could study his grip and movement up close.” Rio was practically bursting with energy. 

Agatha loved the way Rio showed her excitement so forthrightly. She didn’t try to hide her joy or temper her feelings. It was such a refreshing contrast to the way Agatha had been raised and the standards of the time for women. 

On the ride back to Kenosha, Rio sat up front with Doc and they gushed over Satchel Paige’s long list of unique pitches. Peggy and Agatha chatted quietly in the backseat. 

“Thomas from the fire department asked me out on a date tonight. He said one of his co-workers is single, handsome, and would love to tag along if you join. What do you say?” Peggy proposed. After their conversation at the lake house, she had been trying to find potential suitors for Agatha. 

“How old is he? I don’t want to waste my time with some twenty-something.” Agatha said. 

“He’s thirty. Was engaged at some point but didn’t go through with it. Loves baseball. I’ll be there with you, what could it hurt?” Peggy saw Agatha looking for any excuse to say no. 

“Are you going out later, Agatha?” Rio stopped her conversation and turned around to look over her shoulder. “I’ve got a spare ticket to the cinema. Lupe was meant to go with me but isn’t feeling well. I was going to ask if you were interested.” 

Agatha didn’t have to think too hard, “Sure, Rio. That sounds way more fun than a blind date with some firemen. See if Helen or Wanda will go with you instead, Peggy.” 

She couldn’t see Rio’s wide smile as she turned back around and kept talking with the coach the rest of the ride home. 

Coach dropped them off at their host house. Rio leaned out the window and said, “I’ll come by at 6, and we can walk together to the movies.” Agatha nodded and waved as the car pulled away. 

“I can’t believe you’re ditching me.” Peggy huffed as they walked up to the front door. 

“Sorry, I’m just not in the mood to suffer through small talk with some townie.” Agatha said. 

“Welcome back, how was the game?” Gertie looked up from her knitting. 

“It was a blast! We’ll also both be out tonight, so no need to save us a seat at the table.” Peggy knew that Pearl would be upset if they skipped out on dinner without letting them know. 

There was only two hours until they were both set to leave. Agatha threw herself into her bed to relax, while Peggy began the long process of primping and preening for a date. 

“So, what’s going on between you and Rio?” Peggy asked as she applied her eyeliner delicately. 

Agatha flipped over and sat up against the headboard, ‘What? We’re just going to the movies.”

Peggy looked at her roommate via the mirror and leveled a knowing gaze. 

Agatha stared back and finally broke the silence, “What are you suggesting?” 

“I’ve been around the block enough times to spot chemistry, and you two have enough chemistry to form an atomic bomb.”

Agatha laughed aloud, “We’re just friends! Can’t two friends go out to the movies together?” 

Peggy put down her pencil and shifted in the stool to face Agatha, “You can’t tell me that you don’t see it! The way she watches you, the way you stare at her, how she hangs on your every word, how you always end up together. Come on, she’s smitten with you! And if I didn’t know any better, I’d say you were dizzy with her.” 

“But she’s a…she!” Agatha threw her head back against the hardwood behind her and raised her arm to cover her eyes. 

“And? I knew you were self-involved, but have you really not noticed that like a quarter of this league is queer?” Peggy asked. 

Agatha dropped her arm and looked over at her friend, “What? How do you know?” 

“How do you not know?” Peggy threw her arms up in exasperation and went back to putting eyeshadow on. “Remember when we were on the Peaches? If you took your head out of your journal every now and then, you would have noticed half of those gals were dating each other or other ladies in Rockford.” 

“But…isn’t it illegal? It’s not natural. I’m not…I mean I’ve never…” Agatha’s mind was blown by this revelation. 

“Just because it’s not accepted doesn’t mean it’s wrong. This country is so puritanical about sex.” 

“You don’t think it’s bad?” Agatha asked. She was so conflicted. In her mind, the idea of being with a woman seemed wrong. Maybe it was all the fire and brimstone sermons that she had attended as a child, or the constant barrage of negative news stories about ‘deviants.’ 

“I think if two women love each other, then who am I to say they shouldn’t? It's hard enough to find love in this world. If they would risk their wellbeing, their jobs, their reputations, just to be with each other, then they deserve to be happy.” Peggy said. She could see Agatha struggling internally and wanted to provide the kind words that could maybe help her on her way. 

“And you think Rio’s willing to risk that for…me?” 

“I don’t know. I can’t speak for her, but I think you owe it to her and to yourself to see if it’s something. You said you wanted to find love one day, what if you’ve just been excluding half the population?” Peggy applied a bright pink rouge to her cheeks, as if she were completely unbothered at the enormous suggestion she has just given. 

“Okay, so if I take your advice…not saying I will…but if I did, what next? I can’t just tell her all this.” Agatha knew Rio like women. She just really hadn’t considered that she might be part of that category. 

“I know you know how to flirt. The way you speak to Wanda sometimes borders on indecent. And I’ll pick out your outfit. There’s no way I’m letting you step out in a raggedy old frock.”

When Rio rang the doorbell at 5:55pm, Agatha ran to get the door before anyone else could butt in and pepper Rio with endless questions. She threw open the door and slipped out with a hasty “Goodbye!” before striding down the driveway towards downtown. 

“Whoa, Agatha. Wait up!” Rio spun on the stoop and trailed after her companion who had left her in the dust. “I like your outfit. That color looks great on you.” Peggy had picked out a green crepe de chine dress with strong shoulders and a mildly titillating v-neck.   

Agatha slowed down to let Rio catch up, “Thanks. That’s a nice dress.” She admired the bold red color that matched Rio’s lipstick. 

It was a decent trek to the picture house, but it was a warm night and the sun had yet ot set, “What movie are we seeing anyway?” Agatha asked. 

“The Amazing Mr. X. It’s a horror thriller, I hear it’s a hair-raiser!” 

“Oh gosh, I’m not a big horror fan.” Agatha said nervously. 

“Don’t worry, I’ll hold your hand through the scary parts.” Rio admitted with a smile. 

Agatha grinned back. Okay, maybe she is actually interested in me. How did I not notice this before?

“Is this how you swoon all the girls?”

“Just the special ones.” Rio winked and Agatha felt her stomach swoop. 

Oh.

Chapter 14: Going, going, gone

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“World War II was the really big one for my generation. . . . Times changed, women had to leave the home and the kitchen. Now that the men are coming back, you women get back in the kitchen! I’m sorry, you’ve opened the door of opportunity and we’re not in the kitchen, we’re out in the world being productive and doing other things and having other opportunities.”

Delores “Dolly” Brumfield

 

In the tight recording booth, Agatha and Rio were sitting next to each other across from a well-groomed, smooth talking radio host. 

“While women across the country are getting back to their household duties and graciously giving up their positions to returning veterans, there is one place where ladies are still on top. The All-American Girls Professional Baseball League is still going strong here in the Midwest, and today I’m interviewing two of its top stars, Agatha Harkness and Rio Vidal from the Kenosha Comets.” David O’Connell, host of WXRP-Chicago, had invited a few players to the studio at the local station to help boost interest in the upcoming playoffs. 

“Thanks for having us, Davey.” Agatha leaned into the microphone. She had been on the radio a few times and enjoyed the attention. 

“The pleasure is all mine. As a sports journalist, it's not often that I get the opportunity to sit with such lovely ladies like you and Ms. Vidal. Now, my first question, how long have you been playing pro ball?” 

Rio scooted her chair forward and pulled the mic towards her, “This is my rookie season. I was helping to support my family back in Florida, so I wasn’t able to try out prior to this year.” 

“Wow, and now you’re heading to the playoffs with the Comets! What about you, Agatha?”

“I’ve been fortunate enough to play in this league since its inception five years ago. I’ve never won a championship before, so I hope this year is my year.” 

“Your team has a really impressive record, and there are only 8 more games in the regular season. From the looks of things, it seems like you are the favorites.”

“You know baseball, Davey. It’s never as easy as it seems. We’re lucky to have an incredible pitcher like Rio here, but all the top teams this year have good bullpens and even better hitting lineups. We’re going to have to give it our all every single game to make it to the finals.” Agatha said. 

“Well said. What do you say to the people who say women shouldn’t be playing baseball? I know there are many who argue this sport should be left to the men.” 

Agatha tried to keep a calm face despite the rage building inside her. She felt Rio’s hand on her thigh under the table, which didn’t help lower her heart rate. “I would say that those people should come to one of our games before they pass judgement. We can pitch, hit, run, field, and play just as good as the men. And our games only cost a fraction of a major league ticket. It’s the perfect entertainment for the whole family.” 

“Baseball is the national pastime, why should we be excluded from it just because of our gender?” Rio added. 

Davey nodded, “That’s a fair question and a more than fair proposition. If you want to see what these gals are talking about, take a drive over to Kenosha this Thursday through Sunday at 6pm nightly as the Comets face off against the Blue Sox. My listeners can enjoy 25 cents off the regular admission if you mention Davey sent you!”

The producer gave the thumbs up and the recording light turned off. Davey turned to them, “Great work and good luck on your games. We’ll have to have you back on if you win it all.” Agatha agreed and shook his hand. Rio moved to shake his hand as well and Agatha immediately missed the warmth on her thigh. 

They hadn’t discussed what was happening between them yet. After their movie date, where Agatha had spent most of the night covering her eyes and gripping Rio’s hand as if it were her only tether to the world, they hadn’t had a moment alone. 

But something had shifted. 

It didn’t even need to be said. They both felt the change. It was like they were now teetering on the edge of a cliff. They hadn’t tumbled off together yet, but it was now a precarious balance. It felt like it could go either way. 

At practice that evening, Rio was generous with her touches - from subtle squeezes of the shoulder in the locker room to lingering hand holds after rousing high-fives. Agatha didn’t pull away despite every voice in her head wondering if this was right or wrong. 

“Flo, you’re going to start tomorrow’s game. Let’s show these Blue Sox who they are dealing with. Have a good rest, and see you back here tomorrow.” The coach said before dismissing them. 

After most of the team had cleared out, Rio grabbed her bag and made for the exit. She stopped at the payphone along the street to make a quick call. 

“Jen?” 

“Rio! I thought you lost my number, where the hell have you been?” 

“Sorry, it’s been nonstop. We’re going to the playoffs! We just have a few more games to determine our standing.”

“I knew you could do it! See what you can accomplish when you aren’t distracted by pretty girls.” Jen said. 

“About that…” Rio began. 

“No! Please don’t tell me you’re still hung up on that catcher.” 

“I think she likes me back, Jen. No, don't scoff at me. I’m serious. We went out last night to the movies, and she held my hand. She goes out of her way to spend time with me.” Rio felt light and floaty at the thought of Agatha. 

“What if she’s just being nice?” Jen questioned. 

“Agatha Harkness is not just nice. She couldn’t fake being nice if her life depended on it.” 

“Well, why is she wasting time with you?” 

“Ha-ha. Not funny. I’m going to tell her how I feel.” Rio had been holding it back for so long now. She didn’t know how much longer she could wait. 

“I can’t very well stop you, but are you sure? You don’t have to do this. What if you throw this all away? What if you get kicked out of the league?” 

Rio paused and considered it. Getting paid to play baseball professionally was all she ever dreamed about, all she had ever wanted for her life. “Ugh, why do you have to be such a fire extinguisher?” 

“I’m your voice of reason. You can thank me later. It’s late here, I’ve got to wake up early for work in the morning. Not all of us live such comfortable lives! Remember when you prayed for this job, don’t throw it away now!” 

“Talk to you later.” Rio hung up, more conflicted than she had been at the start of the call. She knew that Agatha was interested, that she was opening up to her, that she was letting her in. There was such a dramatic change in the way they interacted now compared to when they had first met. Rio knew it wasn’t simply platonic. 

But was Agatha ready for more? Did she truly understand the risks? Did she want just a fling or did she want something more? 

Rio didn’t want to be just another experiment, especially not when the consequences could be devastating. 

If the Comets won two of the games against the Blue Sox, they would clinch the top spot definitively. The stands were packed, thanks in part to the increased promotion and excitement about the upcoming playoffs. 

Flo led them to an easy 3-0 victory in the first game on Thursday night. Agatha went three for four at the plate, and Dottie hit a killer triple in the seventh inning. Rio had been their biggest cheerleader on the bench as she rested her arm, preparing for her next start. 

Friday night games were always incredibly popular. As folks finished their work week and kids finished school, they loved to come down to the ballpark for a cheap hotdog and a rousing game of baseball. This Friday was no different. As the Comets entered the dugout, they could hear the overwhelming noise of the fans. 

“Did they give out free tickets or something?” Wanda popped her head out to look around at the filled stands. 

“They’re here for me, I think.” Agatha primped her hair and pulled out her lipstick tube to reapply before heading out to the field. 

Rio whispered to Peggy, “Does she really believe that?”

“She doesn’t not believe it.”

“Gather round, gather round.” Coach Grant waved them into a tighter circle, “One more win. That’s it. One win between us and winning the regular season. We can coast to the end if we finish it here. This is the most talented team that I’ve ever been a part of, and I know that we can put this to bed. Who’s with me?” 

The team yelled out together in a satisfying release of collective energy. 

Coach raised his voice to match their intensity, “That’s right! Hands in. Comets on three. One, two, three.”

“COMETS!” 

They were in the field first, and Agatha walked out with Rio in lockstep with each other, already setting that easy rhythm together that would carry throughout the game. 

“You’ve got this. Don’t focus on the crowd, just look at me, okay? Focus on me.” Agatha could tell that Rio was taking in the loud racket around them. 

Rio glanced over slowly, and their eyes met. It was a moment of calm in the middle of a hurricane. Despite their bodies carrying them forward in separate directions, all they could see was each other in that singular pause before it all began.

Agatha brought her caged mask down over her face but kept her eyes trained on the pitcher standing fifty feet away. 

Corky Arnold was the first batter for South Bend, a tall clumsy farmgirl who somehow dominated at first base.  

The first pitch was a high heater at the chest. A perfect kick off to get things going, and Corky didn’t even swing. 

“Ball.” The umpire said without emotion. 

What? Agatha turned to look at him because that pitch was close but should have been a strike. She had well and truly caught enough to know the difference. She didn’t recognize the man standing behind her. Must be a new guy, maybe he’s still finding his zone. 

She called for a change-up next. Rio had excellent placement with this pitch and could paint the corners of the strike zone. The windup, the pitch. 

“Ball.” 

Agatha scoffed aloud. Even the batter looked back in confusion. That pitch had been just slightly inside but level with the batter’s belly button. Agatha looked to her coach who was also looking puzzled. 

“Hey blue!” A man in the stands behind home plate shouted, “I’ve seen potatoes with better eyes than you!” 

Agatha smiled behind her mask. Hecklers could be a pain in the butt when they had their sights set on you, but when they went after the umps it was pretty entertaining. 

Let’s really test him. Agatha dropped a single finger for another fastball, down the middle. As the ball came in Corky swung with all her might and missed. The ump called a strike due to the swing, so Agatha called the same pitch again. 

This time the ball left Rio’s hand and smacked into the catcher’s mitt with ferocity, bang on target. 

“Ball.” 

Agatha jumped up and turned around, “That was a strike.” 

The umpire removed his mask, “I called it a ball. It was high.” 

“I don’t know what you were looking at, but that was dead center.” Agatha argued back. 

“I suggest you turn around and get back to the game.” He had his hands on his hips and had a good five inches on her as he stared Agatha down. 

She knew a losing game when she saw one and bit down on her bottom lip, crouching back down behind the plate.

Rio was tossing the ball up and down to herself, waiting for the game to restart. Agatha could see the frustration growing in the pitcher. She called for a curveball. 

Corky connected this time and sent a weak ground to the shortstop who tossed it easily to Wanda at first for an out. 

Janet James was up next. The first pitch was a fastball, Agatha barely had to move her glove to catch it. 

“Ball.” 

Rio kicked the dirt next to the mound in anger at the call. That should have been a strike. 

A fan screamed out, “Hey ump! I’ve heard better calls between two tin cans and a piece of string!” To which, many in the crowd and the dugout laughed. 

“Time!” Agatha called and put her hand up to stop the game. She turned and took her mask off again. “You’re joking, right?”

The umpire looked to be in his 50s, hard-faced and hulkling. “Look missy, where’s your coach? I’ll speak to him about any issues with my judgement.” 

Agatha stomped along the third base line to fetch the coach, “He will only talk to another man.” She spat out. 

Coach Grant accompanied the catcher back and said, “Is there a problem?”

The umpire crossed his arms, “Your catcher is questioning my calls.”

“If she didn’t, I was about to.” 

“Excuse me?” 

“I can tell you’re new around here, but this is a professional league. The All-American Girls Professional Baseball League. We expect professional umpires too.” Coach Grant knew this man’s type. The way he was looking at the players with disdain gave him away instantly. 

The umpire opened and closed his mouth. Whatever he had expected the coach to say, it wasn’t this. He pointed out to the pitcher, “But sir, she’s not even American.”

Agatha had stepped away to give them space but at that comment she whirled right around and bounded over, “What the fuck did you just say?”

Some fans gasped in the crowd and both Rio and the batter ran over. The umpire growled, “You can’t speak to me like that!” 

“If you’re going to call this game like a racist pig then I can damn well speak to you however I want.” Agatha snarked as she stood toe to toe with the ump. She could see his rapidly reddening face and questioned for just a second whether she had taken it too far. 

“You’re out! Get off this field!” He screamed and pointed to the dugout with rage. 

Agatha stared and then hawked loudly and spat at his feet into the dirt before striding away to leave. The man seethed at the crude action but had no further power to sanction her. 

“Hey! You can’t throw her out! That’s not fair!” Rio cried out in objection at the scene. 

“Do you want to join her?” The umpire turned towards her, chest puffing now. The crowd was just as fed up with the official and shouted their boos loudly. 

Rio hesitated but then threw her glove down, “I’m not playing if you’re the one officiating.” She followed Agatha’s tracks off the diamond. 

Coach Grant turned his head to shout after her, “Don’t leave. Don’t let Agatha go either. Give me a sec.” 

Rio was panicking internally as she avoided eye contact with the players on the bench and quickly cut through the dugout to the locker room. She saw Agatha opening the door and followed her in. 

The catcher turned, “Rio, what are you doing in here?”

“I got thrown out too.” 

“What??” Agatha’s eyes widened in surprise, “They need you out there. We need this win.” 

“Nobody’s ever stood up for me like that. I wasn’t about to keep playing if that bastard was going to keep calling the game.” Rio said. She still couldn’t believe that Agatha would risk the win for her like this. 

“It was bullshit. He might get away with that in some places, but not here. You don’t deserve that.” 

“Thanks, you shouldn’t have done that. Thank you.” 

“I’d have stood up for any of these girls.” Agatha shrugged a shoulder, trying to play it cool. 

“But would you have gotten thrown out for any of them?” Rio prodded. 

“Who can say? It’s never come up before.” 

“You could just say you like me. It won’t kill you to say you like me the most. This is now the second time you’ve been tossed because of me” Rio poked Agatha in the stomach playfully to goad her. 

Agatha jumped away to try to avoid the ticklish taunts, “Don’t make me regret it, Vidal.” 

Rio started chasing her, and they circled the locker room in a childish game of tag - all their previous problems fading away to a silly little diversion. 

“Hello?” Peggy was standing in the doorway watching the game with a self-satisfied smile on her face. The two women stopped dead in their tracks when they realized they weren’t alone. 

“Sorry to break up…whatever this is, but Coach wants you both back out there. I think he talked down that umpire and either threatened his job or his life if he doesn’t start calling strikes.” Peggy explained. 

Agatha quickly went to pick up her ball cap that had fallen on the ground during their game and the three of them walked back out together. In the dugout, Coach Grant was waiting, tapping his foot impatiently, “Go on, back to it. If he makes one more egregious mistake, we’re all leaving and taking the forfeit.” 

“Yes, sir.” Rio said and grabbed her glove off the bench, someone must have picked it up for her. 

Agatha put a hand on her shoulder, “I’ll be out there with you the whole time, okay?” 

Rio felt her heart jump and nodded shyly as they went up the steps onto the dirt again. The fans roared their approval as their star pitcher and catcher emerged again, signalling the start of the game again. 

Agatha crouched down in her usual spot and ignored the man hovering behind her. Janet was still up to bat, the count still stood at one ball, no strikes. The catcher called for a changeup. 

The ball left Rio’s hand as it crossed her body and travelled a deceptive line right to Agatha’s mitt. 

“Strike.”

The smile on Rio’s face was contagious as Agatha grinned right back. Whatever the coach had said to the numbskull umpire seemed to work because Rio struck out the next two batters in a row to end the inning. 

“Let’s go, team. Get on base, come on.” Coach cheered them on as they grabbed their bats. 

Dottie hit a single and advanced to second thanks to a knock by Wanda. Horsey hit a long flyball to center that was caught, and then Peggy grounded into an unlucky double-play. 

The fans started getting antsy in the eighth inning when the score was still tied at zero. Both teams were fighting so hard on defense that nobody was able to put a run up yet. Rio was throwing as well as ever, but the Blue Sox pitcher was also having a strong night. 

“You’re doing great, Rio. Keep it up. We’ll get ‘em.” Agatha tried to reassure the pitcher as they walked out. 

Unfortunately, Nancy Smith took a chop at a curveball and sent it to the far corner for a triple. Rio’s face fell as she watched the ball roll to the fence and the batter round the bases. Agatha took an extra moment resetting to give Rio a second to catch her breath. She couldn’t lose her nerve now, not with a runner on third. 

Pinky Moore came up next and took two balls before laying down a bunt. The ball popped perfectly and rolled toward the pitcher. Agatha ran to grab it and saw Nancy touch home behind her. Fuck. She fired it to first and was able to get the force out, but the sacrifice bunt had worked, and the Blue Sox were now up by one. 

They got out of the inning without any further damage but now needed to score two to end this. 

Shirley was able to hit a ball towards third and make it to first safely. Then it was Agatha’s turn. 

She gripped the bat loosely, feeling the grain of the wood under her hands, and stared down at the opposing pitcher, Dot Krick. She had been pitching for two seasons now and had a curveball that could cross your eyes, but Agatha had studied her well. 

The first pitch was a low fastball. Agatha could see its trajectory as it came in. She channeled her power, her anger at the close-minded umpire, her confusing pull towards Rio, her desire to win, and loaded her swing with all of these intense feelings. As the ball arrived in the sweet spot, she let it all go. 

“Angel crushes the ball to left field. Watch it soar, folks. Back, back, back. That ball is GONE! Home run!” The announcer in the stadium yelled in excitement as the fans jumped and screamed while Agatha jogged around the bases. 

When she got back to the dugout everyone came to pat her on the back and congratulate her. Billy and Tommy gave her approximately thirty high-fives, they were so excited. 

“How do you hit it so far?” Rio shook her head in disbelief and gratitude. 

“Some of us are just gifted.” Agatha stood tall with her chest out. 

“No, I’m serious.” 

Agatha put her bat down and sat beside the pitcher, “I try to imagine all the emotions in my head as fuel for my body and then if the right pitch comes in, that’s like the spark that ignites it all. So much of this game is mental. You have to see it and make it happen.” 

They held the Sox in the top of the ninth inning and were up to bat again. They just needed one run to walk it off and end the game. 

Fossey struck out swinging. Then Buckets hit a solid single. Rio was up next. 

“Go on, Reaper! You got this!” Wanda cheered her on. Agatha watched nervously. 

Rio stood in the batter’s box and got set. She thought of Agatha’s advice and tried to conjure powerful feelings. She thought about placing first in the league, about winning it for her team, about Agatha’s smile, about Agatha’s hair, about Agatha’s hands, Agatha, Agatha, Agatha. 

Crack

The sound ripped her from her obsessive spiral, and she couldn’t believe it as the baseball took off in the air. At some point, she must have swung the bat. 

“Run! Run, Rio!” Someone called from the dugout, which forced her to start running to first. 

The announcer’s voice shouted, “And that ball is outta here! It’s another home run for the Comets! The first one for the pitcher, Rio “the Reaper” Vidal. They’ve won it, it’s all over. The Comets win! The Comets win!” 

As Rio rounded third, the entire team poured out onto the field to meet her at home. When she touched the plate, Agatha was there, lifting her up in a tight embrace as the rest of the team joined into a group hug. 

She felt the catcher’s breath against her ear despite the commotion surrounding them, “Attagirl.” 

And Rio gasped and felt her heart pound just as hard as it had when her bat had connected with the ball. 

When she pulled back, Agatha gave her a swift kiss on the cheek before the team swept her up on their shoulders and carried her around the field in joyous celebration. As fans cried out her name and people stretched to wave at her, Rio was too lost in the tender feeling of Agatha’s lips on her skin to care much about anything else. 

They went on to win the remaining two games against the Blue Sox. The Comets were going into the playoffs as the number one seed in the league. There was just one series left on the road before the postseason began, but they could take it easy now. 

“Your room assignments for the Grand Rapids trip are on the board. Season’s almost over, no complaining.” Lilia droned out after posting the handwritten paper up in the locker room. 

Agatha didn’t bother to rush over, she knew she would be with Peggy as usual. 

“What the…” Peggy ran her finger down the list, “Why am I rooming with Dottie?” 

Agatha’s head snapped up, “What?” She ran over to the list and scanned for her name. Agatha Harkness was written in Lilia’s neat cursive right beside…Rio Vidal. 

“Hey Roomie.” Rio sidled up beside her, looking at the list. 

“What…how did you do this?” Agatha narrowed her eyes at the smug pitcher. 

“I thought you said a magician never reveals their secrets.” Rio snarked back. In reality, she was now the owner of three sets of Tupperware that she would never use thanks to one of Lilia’s many side hustles. But if a bit of plastic was all that stood between her and a room with Agatha, it was worth it. 

Agatha contemplated chasing the old broad and demanding her normal road roommate but knew it was a waste of time. “You better not snore.” Was all she could manage. 

“You know I don’t, dear.” Rio said, thinking back to their time at the lakehouse. 

The four hour bus ride felt extremely long as they traversed the long road around Lake Michigan. Peggy and Agatha were sitting next to each other while Rio sat with the pitchers in the back. 

“Do you want to play neck, screw, or wed.” Rio leaned over the seats and asked them both. 

Agatha spun around, “Sure, why not?” Peggy sat up on her knees as well. 

“Okay, neck, screw, or wed: Coach, Lilia, and…Mr. Wrigley.” Lupe proposed the first three victims. 

“Ooooooh this one’s easy. Neck Coach, screw Mr. Wrigley, wed Lilia.” Agatha said. 

“What? You’d kiss the coach??” Rio asked. 

“I’m not about to screw him or marry him, doll.” She replied to the laughter of the others. 

“I would go: neck the gum man, screw Lilia, wed Coach. I mean surely I’m not the only one who has imagined our chaperone is a real expert in the sack.” Peggy looked at them expectedly but everyone else stared at her in shock. “Well, guess that was just me then…”

“I’ve got one: Bing Crosby, Clark Gable, and Cary Grant.” Wanda had overheard the game and wanted to join. 

“Neck Cary, screw Bing, wed Clark.” Rio said. 

“Why would you marry Clark? That man gets divorced more often than you get hits at bat.” Agatha cracked up at her joke. 

“The right answer is neck Clark, screw Cary, marry Bing.” Wanda said, “Haven’t you heard what they say about Cary Grant? Apparently he is very, very well-endowed.” 

“How do you know that??” Peggy looked at her aghast. 

“Here’s a tough one, Angel. Wanda, Peggy, and Rio.” Lupe said with a sly smile. 

Agatha immediately blushed, “No way, that’s not fair.” 

Betty jumped in at this point, “Awww, come on! I’ll do it: neck Wanda, screw Rio, wed Peggy.” 

“Thanks, dear. I’d marry you too if given the choice.” Peggy reached out to grasp Betty’s hand. “Your turn, Agatha.” 

“It’s just a game!” Wanda yelled.

“Fine! Neck Peggy, screw Wanda, wed Rio.” She mumbled the words out so fast that everyone strained to hear her. 

“Wed who? Me?” Rio pointed to herself. 

Peggy and Wanda started humming the classic “here comes the bride” tune as Agatha sunk down in her seat to try to hide her face. 

“I don’t want a diamond ring. I’d prefer jade, that’s my favorite gemstone, if you’re taking notes.” Rio peered over the seat and offered her preferences to her pretend fiancée. 

“Anything for you, sweetheart.” Agatha played along now as the other players started laughing at the acting. She sat back up and turned so she and Rio were facing each other over the seat. She reached forward to tuck a bit of Rio’s hair behind her ear.  

“And we’ll need to practice the wedding kiss beforehand. I don’t want you to embarrass yourself in front of our guests.” Rio was leaning into the fantasy and staring deeply into Agatha’s blue eyes. 

“Oh hush, you know that won’t be a problem. I’ve never had stage fright before. I don’t choke under pressure.” Agatha gave her that signature wink that made Rio’s heart melt. 

“You two are so funny! You really sound like a real couple.” Betty was cracking up in her seat at the performance. 

“Yeah, you could have fooled me!” Peggy said with a hint of sass. 

After many more silly games, heated discussions, and gas station bathroom breaks, they pulled up to the Grand Rapids Plaza Hotel at 4pm. 

“Games in two hours so get ready in your rooms, then everyone better be back down here and ready to go at 5.” Coach Grant said as they filed off the bus and grabbed their keys from Lilia. 

The rooms were run of the mill standard. Two twin beds, side tables, a dresser, and an ensuite. Agatha threw her suitcase down near the end of the bed she claimed closest to the door. Rio had stayed in the lobby to have a short meeting with the pitchers about tonight’s game. 

Agatha laid down and stared at the unmoving ceiling fan. God, it’s hot in here. She stood to pull the cord on the fan but couldn’t find one. She stood on the bed but couldn’t see it anywhere. She searched the walls for a switch and none of them worked on the fan. She went to the window and pried it open, but there was no breeze. She could feel the sweat on her back already from just walking around the room. This is going to be miserable. 

She must have fallen asleep in the heat because the next thing she knew Rio was standing over telling her it was time to go. 

The first game against the Chicks was uneventful. Coach decided to start the benchwarmers so Agatha and Rio both got a break. Even with their subs in the game, the Comets still won easily 4-0. They didn’t need the wins, but the team loved the competition. 

After the game, back at the hotel, once the adrenaline of a game wore off, the players normally crashed. Unfortunately for both Agatha and Rio, riding the bench wasn’t the most strenuous or exciting activity. As they lay side by side in the sweltering room, neither could fall asleep. 

“I don’t think I’ve ever been this hot before.” Agatha groaned, tossing to her side to try to find any comfortable position that might trick her body into letting her sleep. 

“Why didn’t we ask someone to fix the fan?” Rio stood up on the bed and examined it like Agatha had done earlier. She also could not figure out how to turn it on. 

“Do you think it's dangerous to sleep in the bath? Will I drown in just a bit of water?” Agatha was so tempted by the prospect despite the obvious hazard. 

Rio hopped down off the bed and started ripping the top sheets of the bed, “Come on, I’ve got an idea. Grab your mattress and your pillow.” 

“What are you doing?” 

“You’ll see. Come on!” 

Rio folded the thin, flimsy mattress in half and grabbed her pillow and a sheet. She put it all under her arms and waited for Agatha to do the same. The clock on the wall read it was half past midnight. 

The two players stepped out into the empty hall, and Rio led them to the stairwell. She held open the door with her back as Agatha followed and then they walked the four floors up to the rooftop. When Rio opened the door, which was luckily unlocked, the relief of the open air was immediate. 

“Ahhhhh, god that’s better.” Agatha expressed softly as they carried their bedding to the middle of the roof. She watched Rio lay down her mattress in a clear patch of roof. “Wait, we’re not actually going to sleep up here, are we?”

Rio laid down and patted the ground next to her, “It beats dying of heatstroke in that hotel room, don’t you think?” 

Agatha looked around. She could see the street lamps below lining the surrounding roads and a few building lights, but the night sky looked immense in comparison as it sat overtop of them. “You make a compelling argument.” She relented as she dropped her cargo and got down next to Rio. 

The two of them laid in silence for a long while. Agatha simply stared up at the stars above that looked extra bright and listened to the soft noises of a summer’s night in Michigan. She thought Rio must have fallen asleep after the amount of time that passed, so she jumped when the pitcher whispered her name, “Agatha?”

She turned on her side to face her and saw Rio was staring right back, “I thought you drifted off.” 

“I can’t get enough of the view.” Rio said. 

“You’re looking at me.” 

“Yeah, I know.” Rio smirked and saw the way the compliment washed over Agatha. 

“Oh, you sap.” The catcher gave Rio a weak shove to try to force her to look away but nothing could have forced her to change her gaze. 

There was a heavy air sitting between their prone bodies. An unspoken tension. A delicate feeling of comfortable unease. 

“Agatha?” Rio said her name again like a question. 

“You don’t have to call for me. We’re the only two out here.” 

“I know, I know. I just…wanted to ask you something.” 

Agatha looked at Rio who seemed to be vibrating with anxiety in that moment, “Well? You can ask me anything.”

“Can I kiss you?” 

The question launched into the night air like a firework. The whistling ascent lingering between them as the anticipation loomed. Agatha forced a swallow down her dry throat and looked at the intense brown eyes across from her. Rio was staring at her with a mix of adoration and a guarded sense of anticipatory disappointment, as if something bad might happen at any second. 

Agatha didn’t think about the question. She didn’t consider the implications, the morality of it all, the long-term consequence, or anything. She simply let her heart lead for the first time, and her heart wanted one thing alone. 

When their lips met, it was like the fuse on the firework had finally reached the end. The explosion was instant and fierce. Agatha wrapped one arm around Rio’s back and pulled them together. Rio opened her mouth gently and invited Agatha in. It was as hot as smoking gunpower as their mouths moved against each other in a frantic exchange.

All of the curious questions, the angry contests, the witty conversations. All the longing touches, the yearning stares, the joyful celebrations. The dazzling colors of their past rained down on them in sparkling glory in the quiet of the night. Every moment they shared coalesced into this single, perfect connection as the two women kissed with complete abandon. 

Rio felt like she must have been shot off into heaven because Agatha’s soft lips were on hers. It was everything she had dreamed about for years. From the static magazine picture that she stared at to the hot-tempered real life version that pushed her to the dirt, it was everything and more. A perfect game is when a pitcher pitches a complete game (nine innings) without allowing a single batter to reach a base. No hits, no walks, no errors. Everything has to go perfectly, hence the name. It takes a whole lot of skill but an even bigger amount of luck.

In 1948, in Major League Baseball, there had only been five perfect games ever recorded. Perhaps most famously by Cy Young in 1904, who is often regarded as one of the greatest pitchers of all time.

Agatha’s heart broke a little, “Hey, I don’t know yet. I haven’t told the coach anything yet. I just wanted to let you know where I’m at.”

“Yeah, I get it. What do you think you’ll do - I mean, if you don’t come back?” Rio leaned down to put her shoes on. 

Agatha ran a hand through her hair, trying to make it appear like she hadn’t just had sex all night long, “Go back to the factory I guess. There’s not many options for a gal with only a high school diploma.”

“You could go to college.”

“And study what? I would stick out like a sore thumb amongst all those young people.”

“You could be a teacher.” Rio said it like it was the most obvious solution. 

“What? Why do you say that?” 

“You’re good with kids. I see you with Billy and Tommy. Those kids worship the ground you walk on, they hang on every word you say. And I see you with the younger players and even with me. You are a heck of a mentor. I’ve learned so much just from being around you and the things you’ve shared with me.” 

Agatha didn’t realize Rio paid that much attention to her, “I never thought of it like that. I just hate incompetence and know I can do things better.” 

“You put on a thorny front, but under all those spikes, you care. That’s what makes you good at teaching. You’ll never admit it, but it’s true. I bet you were a great mom too.” 

Agatha almost choked on a sob but tried her best to swallow it down along with all the tears that appeared in her eyes. Keep it together. Keep it together. Change the subject. “I heard you at the end of the game. When you thanked your parents...”

Rio looked away and sat down on the bed, leaving Agatha standing, “I didn’t think anyone heard me.”

“What happened to them?” Agatha moved slowly to sit beside her but maintained a respectful distance.

Rio methodically massaged the palm of her right hand nervously, “I never really knew them. They died when I was just three years old. We were living in Puerto Rico, and consumption was spreading rapidly through the island. They both got sick along with most of the small town we lived in. My mom sent for her sister to come get me as soon as the disease started spreading and that saved my life. She was able to smuggle me on a boat to Florida by pretending I was her child. But I never saw my parents again.” 

“I’m so sorry. That’s awful.” Agatha knew the pain of losing a child so young, but she couldn’t imagine losing both parents as a toddler.

“You know it’s hard to miss what you never had. My aunt and uncle raised me like one of their own. I wish I had known my parents. The main thing I know is that they loved baseball. My aunt told me that my mom used to follow the local team, the Tiburones, on the road and watch all their games. And my dad worked as a ticket taker at the stadium in San Juan. When I play, I feel connected to them.”

“I didn’t know that.” Agatha rubbed her hand in circles on Rio’s back. 

“I don’t like to talk about them. It shouldn’t still hurt this much.”

Agatha felt that deeply, “I still miss Nicky every single day. Time doesn’t make it better, it just dulls the immediacy of the pain.”

“I wish I could stop it. I wish I could make it so less people felt like this.” Rio finally raised her head and looked at Agatha with sad eyes. 

“Everyone dies one day. No matter how we try to fight it.” Agatha’s heart ached at this unfortunate truth. Rio turned and opened her arms. They hugged on the bed and tried to comfort the long ignored wounds in each other. 

“Welcome back lovergirl.” Peggy was reading on her bed in their shared room. 

Agatha had silently crawled through the window this morning. She and Rio had caught the early bus from Racine that dropped them near the stadium. “What did you tell Pearl and Gertie?”

“They didn’t ask. I think Ol’ Gerts was too excited from winning a couple bucks in the betting pool.” 

Agatha breathed a sigh of relief and rummaged through her dresser for a change of clothes. She was still in her dress from last night. 

Peggy shut her book, “So…are you really going to make me ask?”

“It was a ten out of ten.” Agatha bundled up her clothes and made for the bathroom before Peggy could ask any more follow ups. 

When she got back, freshly cleaned and feeling much more put together, Peggy stared her down, “I’m not going to push…yet.” She held up a note in her hand. “Wanda left this in the mailbox for you at some point.”

The dreamy haze around Agatha suddenly dissolved. She grabbed the paper. “It says, ‘meet me at the diner at 10.’ Not much of a wordsmith is she?”

“What did you do?” Peggy asked.

Agatha nervously tried to play it off, “How should I know? Maybe she just wants a heart to heart before the season ends?”

“Well you better run, it’s already half past nine.” Peggy checked her watch. 

Agatha walked to the diner and saw the distinctive redhead sitting at one of the window booths. She sat down opposite her. 

“Agatha.”

“Wanda.”

“Thanks for coming.” Wanda’s voice gave away nothing. She sat still with her hands folded on top of the paper menu. 

“Sure, what did you want to talk about?” Agatha felt her leg bouncing rapidly but couldn’t stop it. She never fidgeted like this.

Wanda grimaced subtly and took a long pause. Agatha felt like the seconds were crawling by. “I think you know.”

Agatha’s eyes darted around. Everyone else in the diner was going about their business. They had no clue that her world was crumbling down, “What do you want me to say?” She finally blurted out. 

“What’s the nature of your relationship with Rio?”

“We’re…” Agatha’s hands were sweating. She rubbed them against her thighs. They hadn’t put a name on what they were. Was there a name for this? Girlfriends? Dating? Going steady? Nothing seemed to accurately describe how it felt. “We’re still figuring it out.”

Wanda clicked her nails on the table. Agatha didn’t know when she found the time to get them professionally manicured given the relentless game schedule on top of twin boys. The redhead tilted her head, “But it’s…romantic?”

Agatha huffed and threw her hands up, “Yes. Is that what you want to hear? What’s with the interrogation, Wanda? You saw us. Are you planning to turn us in, or what?” 

“Aren’t you worried? You’re clearly not being careful.” 

“I didn’t plan on this happening. It just did. I can’t explain it.” Agatha said. 

“These things don’t just happen, Agatha. It’s not right. Two women shouldn’t be together…like that.” Wanda spit the words out. Agatha was shocked at this response. Wanda was the closest thing to family she had on this team besides Peggy. She wasn’t naive, but the reality of the judgement was crushing. 

“I haven’t changed. You know me. Come on, nothing’s changed.” Agatha said. Her voice shook as she tried to salvage this. 

“I don’t want you around my children anymore.”

Agatha gasped. Her heart stopped, “What? You don’t mean that. You can’t…”

“I don’t want you to influence them in any way. Just stay away from us, and I won’t say anything to anyone else.”

“Billy asked when I was going to visit him in New Jersey.” Agatha felt empty. It was all her worst fears coming to life. This was how it was going to be. If she kept pursuing things with Rio, this was how the rest of her life was going to go. 

One painful rejection after another. She didn’t know if she could deal with more loss. 

“You’re no longer welcome. I’m sorry, Agatha. It’s for the children. I can’t have them around a…a…queer.” She whispered the slur like it stung her lips on the way out. 

Agatha sat back like she had been slapped. There was nothing more to say. This was how the world felt about her now. She was something to be feared, something to exclude and remove. 

Wanda opened her mouth to say something but thought better of it and scooted out of the booth, grabbed her bag, and walked away. She knew her message had landed. 

Agatha sat alone in the diner. 

Spiraling.

Chapter End Notes
