Sorry, here comes the angst / period-typical homophobia. I tried to soften the blow with some smut and fluff.

On another note, just to drive home the improbability of a perfect game in baseball. In the 154 years of recorded Major League Baseball history, which accounts for over 238,500 games, there have only been 24 official perfect games! In the 9 years of the AAGPBL, there were five perfect games. It's a crazy achievement.

Also, I'm now on tumblr. Was planning to add some inspiration photos and historical pics for my fics there. Come join if you want!

Chapter 17: Game one

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“I thought I was pretty good back home, and I was. But then I got to spring training and I saw all the other girls playing and I thought ‘wow.’ I was a little fish in a big pond.”

Sue Parsons

Half the team took the two hour trip the next day after practice to Rockford. They were eager to catch game five of the other semi-final match, the Blue Sox vs the Peaches. 

Agatha and Rio sat next to each other in the car the entire way, but Agatha simply stared out the window silently. 

Rio didn’t know what had happened. After their victory the other night and the unforgettable stay in the motel, it felt like everything was going well. Now, Agatha felt distant and cold - like everything that had happened was forgotten. 

“I’ve got a dollar on the Blue Sox winning.” Lupe said as they bought their tickets at the main entrance. 

Dottie laughed, “That’s a long shot! The Peaches are clearly the favorites.” 

“I don’t know, Dottie. South Bend has Corky Arnold. Agatha is still leading the league in home runs, but she is number two. I wouldn’t count them out.” Rio said. 

Agatha just passed her coins over and took her ticket. She didn’t gloat about her record, didn’t offer any snarky remarks, it was so unlike her. 

Rio pulled her to the side before they went through the turnstiles, “Okay, what the hell, Agatha? What did I do?”

The catcher crossed her arms, “Nothing, Rio. I’m fine.”

“You sure don’t look fine. You’re treating me like a stranger. I thought…after everything…I thought we were good.” Rio leaned against the brick wall of the stadium as other excited fans passed by to get into the park. 

Agatha sighed heavily like the weight of the world was pressing down on her lungs, “I just don’t think I can handle this.” 

“Handle what?”

“This! Us!” Agatha uncrossed her arms and threw them into the air but kept her voice from rising too high and drawing attention. “Wanda confronted me.” 

Rio understood then. Agatha wasn’t angry - she was scared, “What did she say?”

“She doesn’t want me around the twins anymore.” Agatha said. The pain in her tone was evident. She had already lost one child in her life. 

Rio clenched her fists and felt her jaw tick with tension, “She’s wrong.”

“No she’s not. What we’re doing…it’s wrong.”

“You don’t mean that.” Rio’s heart was slowly crumbling. This couldn’t happen. Not again. 

“The way Wanda feels, that’s how everyone else feels. You’re kidding yourself if you think otherwise.” Agatha said. 

Rio shook her head, “I don’t think that’s true. I know how I feel about you, Agatha. I don’t want to live in a world where I don’t get to feel like this.” She hated how desperate she sounded. 

“Well, well, well. If this isn’t a sight for sore eyes.” A new voice cut into the fray. They both looked up and saw two familiar faces striding towards them. 

Rio rushed towards Greta and Carson with her arms wide. She hugged them both fiercely. They had no idea how much she needed this distraction right then. 

“What are you two doing here?” Rio asked when she finally stepped back. 

“Our season on the road with the Sallies ended two weeks ago. We wanted to cheer on the Peaches again. Are you checking out the competition?” Carson guessed. 

“Yeah. You remember Agatha, and a few other Comets are already in the stands.” Rio said. 

“Hey there, Angel.” Greta said with a flirtatious wave.

Agatha had zero desire to socialize right now but didn’t seem like she had much choice, “Greta, Carson, how’s it going?”

“Oh you know, we’re already in the off-season. Back to the boring reality of civilian life.  Can’t believe the Comets are going to finals. We’d kill to be in your position now. I could really use that cash bonus to prolong my return to rent and bills.” Greta said. She lived in California and worked as a production assistant on movie sets. 

“You doubted us?” Agatha asked with a smile, finally feeling a little more alive. 

“I never doubted Rio here. You’re damn lucky you got this gal on your team.” Greta put an arm around Rio’s shoulder. Agatha felt a surge of jealousy hit her in the gut like a sucker punch.

“What about the rest of us? Just chopped liver?” 

“Rio’s special. I think she could carry any team in this league to the finals on her back.” Greta’s hand slowly retracted and paused at Rio’s neck to play with her curls, which did little to tame the green monster in Agatha. 

One second ago she had been ready to end things, but now she bristled at the thought of another woman’s hands on what belonged to her. Stupid, mushy heart.  

“I think we better take our seats. Right, Rio?” She reached out to grab the pitcher’s hand. 

“Uh, yeah. Will we see you guys after?” Rio asked her former teammates. 

“Meet us here after the game. We know a place in town that you might like - that you both might like.” Carson said with a wink. 

Rio let herself be led by the hand by Agatha, who was all but stomping to the entrance. They got through and easily found their seats along the first base side, towards the back, the rest of the team was already seated. The two took the final spots on the bench near the steps. 

The announcer started his usual pre-game spiel. 

Rio leaned over, “What was that about? I thought you were saying we shouldn’t do this anymore.”

Agatha turned her head, “We’re not doing anything.”

Rio’s eyes narrowed, “You looked like you were about to take a swing at Greta.”

Agatha’s head felt like a jumble of puzzle pieces. Nothing was matching up. She knew how she felt about Rio. She knew it was wrong. Or that everyone thought it was wrong. But the way it felt was like nothing she had ever experienced. She knew Wanda hated her now. She didn’t want to lose a close friend. She didn’t want to jeopardize her career. But seeing Greta touch Rio…it had made her forget all that. 

Rio was hers. She wanted Rio to be hers alone.

“My head says we should stop.” Agatha whispered. 

“And your heart?” 

“I need more time.” 

Rio understood. She knew the realities of the world. It could be cruel and unyielding for women like them. Agatha was new to this. She was trying to protect herself, and Rio couldn’t fault her for that. She carefully laid her hand on Agatha’s, “I’ll wait for you - as long as you need.”

The game was pretty boring for the first couple innings. It wasn’t until the bottom of the fourth that the Peaches scored two runs off a ground rule double. The packed stadium went crazy, which only encouraged the team further, and they ended up scoring another pair of runs to lead the Blue Sox, 4-0.

It seemed hopeless, but Corky lived up to her reputation and hit a homer in the seventh inning to claw one run back. Their team fought hard and scored another in the eighth, but it wasn’t enough. The shortstop threw out the last Blue Sox batter at first in the top of the ninth to close out the game. 

The Peaches were going to the championship. 

Agatha and Rio told the rest of the team that they were going to hang around town for the night with some old teammates. Lupe decided to join them. She used to play with Greta and Carson a few years ago too. 

“Hey ladies.” Greta waved them over to the parking lot. 

“Lupe! Good to see you.” Carson hugged her, “You coming with us?”

Lupe nodded, “Wouldn’t miss it. You’re taking them to The Office, right?”

“Yes, ma’am. Jump in.” Greta opened the back door of her red Cadillac for them. 

“How do you know where we’re going?” Rio asked her fellow pitcher. 

“I showed Carson this place first, by accident.” Lupe said with a smirk. Agatha had no idea what they were talking about or where they could possibly be going. What office would be open this late?

The drive over as quick as it started. They were near the Rockford cinema, and Greta parked along the main street. 

“Are we seeing a flick?” Agatha asked. 

“We’re not that square. Come on.” Greta looped her arm with Carson’s, and they led the group along the sidewalk. Carson looked both ways before dipping down a side alley. Agatha hesitated but didn’t want to be left alone. 

It must have been around 9pm. There weren’t many people out and about. The alley was dark, and there wasn’t much besides a dumpster and some trash cans. Greta and Carson went up a non-descript wooden staircase that led to an unmarked door beneath a bright blue lightbulb.

Agatha fought against all the voices in her head that said “turn around!” She followed closely behind Rio as they entered the mysterious door. Inside, to her surprise, it looked like they were in someone’s office. There were filing cabinets lining the walls, a dim desk lamp, and a large desk facing them. 

“Tax problems? Because we do tax solutions.” A man in tie and suspenders asked. He was sitting at the chair behind the desk, writing in a logbook, then he looked up. “Oh, Greta. Go right through.”  

“Thanks, Johnny.” 

She opened up what appeared to be a cabinet door on the wall. The group walked into an empty room. This one was curtained and bare of furniture, the plumbing pipes jutted from the brick walls. The soft sounds of a jazz number floated into the room. 

“Okay, what is this place?” Agatha said, exasperated. 

Greta laughed, “It’s a place for us. A place where we can be free.” She approached the far wall and peeled back the curtain. 

Agatha’s jaw dropped as she crossed the barrier, her eyes couldn’t take in the scene fast enough. They entered into what appeared to be a secret club. There was a dance floor, tables and chairs scattered around the space, darts, moody lighting, and a small stage with a piano. Across the opposite wall was a beautiful wooden bar. A haze of cigarette smoke added to the allure. 

She felt Rio pulling at her arm, “What?”

“Look around.” Rio sounded awestruck as she properly took in her surroundings. 

Agatha finally looked past the surprise of the environment and noticed who was occupying the space. It felt like her eyes were about to pop out of her head when she realized. 

Men slow dancing with other men, women cuddled close at a table, women in pants and suits, hands holding hands, brazen kisses on the dancefloor. Was that…Jo DeLuca kissing the Blue Sox relief pitcher? Agatha couldn’t believe it. 

“Pretty sweet, huh?” Carson elbowed her gently. She remembered feeling similarly the first time she found this place years ago. It was like the scene in Wizard of Oz when the world goes from sepia to full technicolor. 

“But…how is this possible? Isn’t this…” Agatha stumbled over her words. 

“Illegal? Technically, yes. But they can’t legislate us out of existence. Did you think you were the only one?” Greta asked, wrapping her arm around Carson’s waist and pulling her close. 

Honestly, a part of Agatha did. Well, besides Rio. Because it was all so hidden, sometimes she felt completely alone. “I had no idea.” 

“Vi opened this joint with her wife, Edie. They’re over there, behind the bar.” Greta pointed to two women pouring drinks. One was dressed in a man’s three piece, pinstripe suit and had a tidy short haircut. She looked to be in her 60s. The other looked around the same age but was in a pretty floral dress, with typical curled, long hair. “They’re huge Peaches fans.”

“Can I have this dance, m’lady?” Rio interrupted her thoughts and extended a hand as a young singer took the stage and began to croon Doris Day’s hit song “It’s Magic.” 

Agatha nodded and took her hand. They walked together to the middle of the floor besides two older gentlemen who gave them a knowing smile. Greta and Carson joined beside them. The lyrics echoed the moment.

Without a golden wand

Or mystic charms,

Fantastic things begin

When I am in your arms

Rio’s arms laced around her waist lightly, and Agatha looped her arms around the pitcher’s neck. They moved slowly to the song, staring into each other’s eyes. 

When we walk hand in hand

The world becomes a wonderland

It’s magic

“Do you think there are more places like this out there?” Agatha asked. 

“If there’s a place like this in little, old Rockford, Illinois, then there must be hundreds or thousands across the country.” Rio reasoned. She couldn’t believe her luck. One moment Agatha had been contemplating cutting her out, and now they were dancing together in front of other people. 

How else can I explain

Those rainbows when there is no rain

It’s magic

“I’m sorry.” Agatha stepped closer and leaned her forehead against Rio’s. She knew it wasn’t enough. Those two words didn’t feel like enough to encompass her regret. 

“I don’t blame you. This isn’t going to be easy. But maybe we could do it. If these other people can make it work, maybe we could too.” Rio wanted that desperately. She wanted to be with Agatha - more than just stolen moments in hotel rooms or empty locker rooms. 

Why do I tell myself

These things that happen are really true

When in my heart I know

The magic is my love for you

When the last note ended, the group joined Lupe at a table along with the Peaches’ left fielder. 

“Martha Everett.” She put a hand up in greeting, though most of them knew her already. 

“So…when did this happen?” Greta motioned between Agatha and Rio. “Last time we saw you, Rio, you were punching Angel in the face.” 

The group burst out laughing. Then Lupe added, “This is also news to me. I suspected something, but I never would have guessed you were one of us, Angel.” 

“She couldn’t resist my charms.” Rio grinned widely. 

Agatha scoffed, “You were obsessed with me. If anything this is an act of charity.”

“Oooh, well we know who wears the pants in this relationship.” Carson joked as Rio feigned hurt at Agatha’s quip. 

“You know, I’ve always wondered, why do they call you Angel?” Martha asked Agatha.

Rio turned her head, “Yeah, I’ve always wondered that too.”

Agatha smiled at the memory, “I thought you would have heard this by now. It’s not that exciting. People used to call me Hark when I first started in the league. It wasn’t until Wanda came along. Every single time Billy heard someone say ‘Hark’, he would bust out singing ‘Hark the herald angels sing!’. That was the only lyric the little 3 year old knew, so he would just repeat it over and over. The girls started calling me Angel just to shut him up!” 

Rio cracked up laughing along with Martha who added, “And here I thought it was because of your good behavior.”

“I’m no saint, honey.” Agatha showed her teeth and her mind immediately went to the debaucherous nights spent in bed with Rio. She didn’t think people would be calling her Angel if they knew about that. 

“How long have you two been together?” Rio saw Agatha drifting off and tried to change the subject to Greta and Carson. 

“Five years. I had my eye on this one since I first saw her at try-outs in ‘43.” Greta said. 

“Wow. And are you together in the off-season or…?” Agatha was dying to know how they made this work for so long. 

“I’m married.” Carson admitted, holding up her left hand to show off the simple gold band. “Charlie’s a good husband. We have an…arrangement. During the season, I’m free to do as I please. When I’m home, I’m his wife.” 

“And you’re fine with this?” Agatha looked to Greta, who was staring sadly at the table. 

“It keeps us safe. We all have to make sacrifices as part of this particular life.” Greta said. 

Agatha thought about her own situation. There was only one week left with Rio. What would she be willing to sacrifice? What would Rio be willing to sacrifice for her? What would they do to be together?

Rio stood on the train platform in Chicago the next day. She had borrowed Horsey’s car for the day, with the promise of a 12 pack of beer in return. She heard the train approaching before being able to see anything. She teetered on her feet in anticipation. 

The carriages rolled past slowly before coming to a stop. She scanned the disembarking passengers, craning to get a view over the crowd. 

“Rio!” 

“Jen!” Rio caught sight of her best friend and rushed to greet her. They collided and almost fell over to the ground. 

“You look different.” Jen noted as she stepped back to take in Rio’s appearance. It had been almost half a year since they had laid eyes on each other. The longest time they’d ever been apart. 

“I feel different. Where’s Uncle Hector?” She scanned the people, searching for her uncle. 

“He was right behind me.” Jen was taller and spun around to locate her travelling companion. “There!” She pointed to a confused gentleman wandering near the bathrooms. 

Rio rushed over, “Tio! You made it!” She jumped into his arms and felt like she was a child again. Hector was 59, only a few inches taller than his niece and the proud owner of an impressively thick moustache. He was still very muscular from years laying bricks and swung Rio around like she weighed nothing. 

“Mija, I missed you so much. I knew you could do this! I’m so proud of you.” He set her down gently and picked his suitcase back up in one hand and put his other arm around her shoulders. 

“I can’t believe I got you two out of Florida. Never thought I’d see the day.” Rio joked and led them to the parking lot. “How was the train ride?”

“Awful! It’s only thanks to your uncle that I wasn’t relegated to the colored carriage. I thought he was going to sock the train inspector who confronted me. Uncle Hector played blind and said I was his carer and needed to sit with him - sneaky devil.” Jen chuckled. 

“I wasn’t about to travel across the country by myself! I get lost walking down my own street. I never would have made it without Jen. I swear I forgot where my seat was about ten times on the trip.” Hector said. 

“You’re terrible! Well, I’m glad you made it regardless.” Rio popped the trunk and got into the driver’s seat. She got all the gossip on the drive to Kenosha. Aunt Marisol was having a feud with the priest over an argument about after-church snacks, her cousin, Chris, was promoted to foreman at his construction job, her littlest cousin, Pascal, was the starting pitcher on his little league team, and Jen had quit the docks and was thinking of becoming an Avon lady. 

“And?” Jen prompted him.  

Rio looked to her uncle and saw him hesitating, “What? What happened?” 

“No, nothing bad.” He reassured her. “It’s just…the bosses cut my hours. And your aunt’s been losing her ironing jobs as other folks have been getting laid off all over the neighborhood.” 

“Oh no. What can I do?” Rio asked. She knew how tight their budget was already. 

“Don’t worry, mi princesa. Christian is helping us out, and Julio just got a part time job at the car wash. We’ll figure it out. We always do.” His demeanor betrayed the confidence of his words. 

“Listen, we get a pay increase for making the finals. I’ll get an even bigger payday if we win it all. I want to help.” Rio knew that the team got extra wages for playing all these extra games. Greta told her about a bonus that accompanied the trophy too, usually around $500 each. 

“No, if you win, then you earned it. Don’t you dare give that away to us.” Hector had on his stern voice. 

Rio pretended to relent but resolved in her mind that any winnings would go straight to her family. She wouldn’t let them suffer due to pride. She wanted to win before, but now she was determined to make it happen. 

“Enough about us. When’s the first game?” Hector asked. 

“Tomorrow night at 6pm. I’m starting games one, three, and five. And then I’ll pitch relief, if needed.” Rio said. 

They pulled into the local motel. Rio had paid for two rooms out of her savings, despite the protests from her guests. She liked being able to treat them, plus she was planning to stay with Jen for the five days that she was in town. 

“I’m meeting some friends for lunch. Do you want to come with us, Uncle Hector?” Rio asked. 

“No thanks, mija. I think I’m just going to have a mid-day nap. I’ll see you later.” He grabbed his case and waved goodbye as Rio and Jen walked back to the car. 

“Who are we meeting for lunch?” Jen asked. 

“Peggy and Agatha.”

“Agatha? Thee Agatha?” Jen was giddy at the prospect. She had heard so much about the mysterious catcher from Rio over the past few months. 

Rio groaned, “Yes, that one. Please don’t embarrass me.”

“Me? I’d never! Do you think she would like to hear about who your first kiss was?” 

“NO! Don’t you dare.”

“What? I was a great kisser. I taught you everything you know.” Jen smacked her lips playfully. 

Rio drove them to the diner and parked near the entrance. She didn’t see Agatha so got a table for four. Rio pointed out her favorite dishes on the menu. 

“I’m starving! I swear all these extra practices are making me ravenous.” Rio could hear Peggy’s distinctive accent the second they walked through the door. 

“I’m getting my own basket of fries. Don’t steal mine this time.” Agatha said as they approached the booth. 

The two slid into the seats, “You must be Jen.” Agatha extended a hand. Rio had warned her they were coming yesterday. 

“You must be Agatha.” 

“You know me?” 

“Rio hasn’t shut up about…OW!” Jen started before Rio kicked her beneath the table. 

Agatha leaned forward over the table, “Oh? What’s this? Rio couldn’t shut up about me?” She was giddy at the thought. 

“No, no, nothing!” Rio tried to ignore it. 

Agatha had on a sinister smile, “So Jen, how long have you and Rio been friends?” 

“Just about as long as I can remember. We lived on the same block and my brother was friends with her cousins. We felt like the only two girls in our whole neighborhood. Granted, she’d rather be playing baseball or football with the guys, but she’d also play house or dolls with me sometimes.” 

“How sweet. And going back to what you said earlier…what has Rio told you about me?” Agatha asked. She could see Rio not so subtly shaking her head at Jen. 

Jen looked at Peggy quickly, wondering if she was able to speak freely. Agatha saw the look, “Peggy knows, don’t worry.”

“Oh, in that case, where to begin! She was so torn up about you from that first game. I thought I was going to gag, it was so sickly sweet.”

“ Jen .” Rio grumbled her name in warning, but it was an empty threat. 

“So many calls I had to listen to about how she didn’t think you’d ever like her. It was such a drag. It was a relief when you finally got together. I didn’t think I could stand her moping anymore.”

Agatha ran her hand along Rio’s thigh beside her, touched at the thought of Rio’s prior obsession, “Awww, she’s pretty cute, right?”

“I almost missed the sad yearning once she started going on and on about your beauty and your lips and-” 

“Okay! That’s enough of that.” Rio cut in again to save herself the embarrassment. 

“It was just getting good!” Agatha whined. 

Jen laughed, “But on a serious note, what are your plans together? Are you gonna come see us in Florida?”

Agatha paused. They hadn’t decided anything. Rio spoke instead, “We’re still figuring it out, Jen. This is all still very new.”

“Fine, fine, but I hope you know, if you hurt Rio, I’m coming for you.” 

Peggy snorted, “Ha! I like you.” Agatha forced a smile despite the real fear that Jen was not kidding. 

After Agatha and Peggy left, Rio and Jen stayed for a while in the diner, enjoying the unlimited drip coffee. 

“I get it.” Jen nodded with wide eyes. 

“What?”

“Agatha. Her whole deal. She’s hot, like actually smoking hot.” 

“Yeah,” Rio fidgeted with her mug, “I’m well aware.” 

“How did she ever fall for a scamp like you?” 

“Maybe I’m just lucky.” And Rio did feel like that was true. 

Game one of the championship was at home in Kenosha. Rio gave Uncle Hector and Jen directions on how to walk to the ballpark and told them to be there a bit early, otherwise they might get locked out. 

“Good luck. Show them what you’re made of.” Hector gave Rio a bear hug and held back his tears. He had always worried about his only girl, but seeing her here, seeing what she accomplished, he was so impressed. 

“Give ‘em hell, Rio.” Jen put a hand on her friend’s shoulder, which felt grounding and helped calm Rio’s growing nerves. 

“I’ll see you guys after.” Rio donned her Comets cap and made her way to the ballpark. 

Along the way, cars honked at her and people shouted their excitement. The whole town was abuzz. Rio felt sudden dread - she didn’t want to let all these people down. She didn’t want to let her family down. 

As the team warmed up in the field, Rio and Agatha practiced in the bullpen. The sun was starting to drop in the sky, and the annoying gnats hovered above them. 

“So, what’s the verdict? Did Jen like me or not?” Agatha asked as they took a short water break together under the shaded awning. 

“She likes you. Maybe a bit too much for my liking.” Rio mumbled the last bit, and Agatha’s smile couldn’t be wider. 

“Are you going to introduce me to your uncle?” 

Rio tossed the ball up and caught it in her glove, “He doesn’t know - about…well, you know. I’ll have to introduce you as just another teammate.”

“I know. I’d still like to meet him.” 

“Alright. After the game, follow me out.”

After a while, Peggy called them over to the dugout where Coach Grant was gathering the entire team. Lilia waved them over, and they stood near the back. 

“This is it. All the grinding, all the sweat, all the hard work has led us to this moment - the finals. There’s not much more to say that I haven’t already said. Don’t let the pressure bring you down. We’re just playing ball. Remember why you love this game. 

Baseball is unlike anything else. It’s the only sport where we aren’t playing against time. There’s no clock, no countdown. Just you and your teammates fighting for three outs or fighting to stop the other team from getting three outs. Three outs. That’s it. 

The game can change on a dime. A team could score a hundred runs between outs two and three. So never let up. I don’t care if we’re leading by one run or ten. Let’s run up that score. No mercy!”

“No mercy!!” The team screamed with fire in their eyes. The battle cry they clung to for salvation. 

“Quite the pep talk there, Coach.” Agatha said while adjusting the straps on her chest protector. 

“Too much?” He cringed slightly. He had never been much of a fire and brimstone type leader. 

“No, I think it was just what they needed to hear. I agree, mercy is overrated.” 

The Comets ran to their positions in the field and got ready for the first batter. Rio felt all the eyes on her. The stands were completely full. Even the field past the fences was packed with fans hoping to catch a home run ball. She couldn’t make out any individuals, it looked like a rolling mass of bodies in every direction. 

She took comfort in the knowledge that Jen and her uncle were somewhere amongst the crowd. Agatha looked as calm as ever, but Rio knew that the catcher had only slept two hours last night. She had burned the midnight oil stressing over this game. 

When the right fielder, Judith, walked over and settled into the batter’s box, Rio was ready. She was sick of the waiting and the nerves. Time to rip off the bandage. Agatha called for a fastball right out of the gates. She wanted to make an immediate statement. 

Rio accepted the sign. She took in a deep breath and started her windup. As she kicked out her legs, she released the breath and hurled the ball with all her might. It zipped across the plate as Judith swung right over the top of it. “Strike.” 

The crowd applauded loudly as the game got underway. 

The first two outs were easy. The third batter was the catcher, Carol Green. She was a long ball threat. The blonde had a low stance and waggled her bat as she waited for each pitch. Agatha knew her well. She called for a changeup, which Carol was too fast on and fouled off to the left. A curveball came next, which was a ball, a touch too low. 

The fastball was right on target, but so was Carol’s bat. The crack reverberated in Agatha’s ears as the ball launched skyward toward left field. 

Shirley tracked it backwards, running while trying to keep an eye on it over her shoulder. Unfortunately, she misjudged it and the ball dropped just at her feet. She scrambled to recover it and toss it to Peggy for the cut off. Carol had the wheels to make it to second though for a double. Agatha saw Rio’s body language drop and knew she was upset at this early setback, but she wasn’t worried yet. 

The next batter popped up a foul ball behind the plate, which Agatha caught for the final out, preventing the Peaches from scoring. 

The catcher spoke low to Rio on their way into the dugout, “Don’t show your frustration so plainly. They’ll pounce on any sign of weakness.”

“Sorry, sorry. It feels like my fault sometimes.” Rio confessed. 

“These are the best batters in the league. They’re bound to get a few hits, alright?” 

The pair walked down the steps. Agatha was immediately confronted by the twins, “Great catch, Auntie Aggie!” Billy yelled. 

Agatha immediately searched for Wanda, who was already rushing over. “Boys, come over here.” She said sharply. 

“But mom!” Billy whined and reached out for Agatha’s hand. 

“Don’t touch him!” Wanda snapped and quickly pulled the boy towards her. 

“Hey, calm down.” Rio moved to stand between them, trying to protect Agatha from Wanda, who resembled a fierce mama bear all of a sudden. 

“I thought I told you to stay away from them.” Wanda pointed a finger accusatorily towards the catcher. 

“Whoa, what’s going on?” Peggy stepped into the space as the rest of the team turned to stare. They may not all be best friends, but everyone treated each other with respect. This was very unusual. 

“Mom?” Billy looked sadly at his mother and then at Agatha, who couldn’t stand to see the hurt look on the young boy’s face. It was too painful. It brought back too many memories. 

“Come on, son.” Wanda ushered him to the far side of the space, turning her back on everyone else. 

“Are you alright?” Rio put a hand on Agatha’s back, which she flinched away from. 

“Forget about it. I’m fine.” 

Coach Grant leaned over from his spot on the steps. “Is there a problem?”

Agatha was silent as she threw herself down on the bench and stoically watched Dottie head out to lead off the batting order. Peggy simply sat beside her and shook her head at the coach, trying to convey the message - don’t ask .

The team got two singles, but the Peaches pitcher, Grace Nickelson, struck out two in a row and Dottie got thrown out at third. 

The next inning was quick on defense. Rio set a relentless pace, and Agatha didn’t let the encounter with Wanda throw her off her game either. They sat down the batters in succession. On offense, Agatha was first to bat. She popped one up to the outfield right in the gap between right and center. It fell for a single as they got it in quickly. 

Coach Grant gave her the signal for a steal. Fossey was up next. Agatha waited for the right moment. The second the Peaches pitcher started her wind up, she took off towards second base. She tracked the ball out of her peripherals and saw the catcher had it. She slid hard, face first, and hit the base before the second baseman tapped her with the glove. 

“Safe!” The field ump shouted as he crossed and uncrossed his arms. The rush of adrenaline was pulsing through her as Agatha jumped up and pumped her fist. 

She could barely feel the raw skin of her hands and arms that had scraped against the dirt to carry her to her destination. 

Fossey performed a sacrifice bunt to advance Agatha to third. Then, Buckets nailed a worm burner right past the shortstop, which sent Agatha home for the first run of the game. 

Rio was waiting in the on deck circle and gave her a high-five, “Way to run those bases, Angel.” 

“Keep the rally going, slugger.” Agatha grasped the pitcher’s hand and gave it a squeeze. Rio pulled back and saw blood on her palm. Her eyebrows raised in surprise. Agatha didn’t realize her hands were bleeding from the slide. Before she could apologize, Rio simply brought her own palm to her mouth and licked the blood off in one seamless swipe like a freak. 

Agatha shouldn’t have been so turned on. But seeing Rio’s tongue like that…

She felt the warmth painting her cheeks red and fled the field for fear that someone might notice. Lilia helped clean and bandage up her hands and the scrapes on her arms. 

Rio got a single but was left on base as the Peaches pulled off an impressive double play on the next hit. 

By the eighth inning, the Comets were up by three runs. The Peaches had scored one in the third but hadn’t been able to create anything since.

“Remember what I said. Don’t let up! Let’s finish them!” Coach Grant kept their energy high as they ran back out there. 

Agatha crouched down in her spot. The exhaustion was starting to hit her. Her mind was starting to wander. Why is Wanda so repulsed by me? Am I really that bad? Am I disgusting? Is she right? I don’t think I can handle this. Billy’s face. He’s just a kid. 

She didn’t fully register the batter now standing in front of her and called for a fastball. Rio took a second and shook it off. Agatha called it again. Rio knew the catcher wouldn’t call it twice unless she meant it. Bobbie loved fastballs, but maybe Agatha knew something she didn’t. 

The ball came in high and fast. Rio saw the deep dimple on Bobbie’s cheek appear as the batter smiled. It was just what she was hoping for. Bobbie swung hard. 

“Back, back. That ball is crushed! It’s a home run for the third baseman, Bobbie Key!” The announcer shouted. 

Agatha ripped off her mask and watched in horror as the ball dropped over the fence and the fans scrambled to grab it. What have I done? Rio was looking at her with confusion. I wasn’t paying attention - fuck. 

The score was Comets 3, Peaches 2. It was close. 

Rio was keeping her cool surprisingly well. Agatha ran a hand down her face and then replaced her mask. She took in the batter fully this time. Oh for god sake. It was Martha Everett. The outfielder that she met at the clandestine gay bar. 

Thankfully, the batter made no acknowledgement of their meeting. She swung at the first pitch, hit a bouncing grounder right to first, and was out. They finished the inning without further damage.

“What happened with you?” Rio confronted Agatha as they sat down on the bench. There was a hint of venom in the question. 

“I got distracted. I’m really sorry. That was completely my fault.”

That seemed to placate Rio for now, “I really want to win this, Agatha. Please.” It wasn’t a request. It was a wish, a tightly held hope. 

“I know. This is all I’ve wanted since I joined the league. I need to win this too.” Agatha admitted.

Chapter End Notes

Got a bit carried away writing this one and kept adding more and more.

If you want to listen to the song they dance to, here's a link (Doris Day - It's Magic). The gay club I reference is from A League of Their Own show, episode 6. The bartender, Vi, is a great cameo from one of the original cast members from the 1992 movie.

Chapter 18: Left on base

Chapter Notes

Just want to say in advance...I'm sorry!!!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

“The opportunity to show that you are good at something, to have people yell their approval of you, injects powerful ingredients into the soul.” 

Morris Markey

 

They won the first game.

How could they not. 

Rio pitched the entire nine innings. She closed it out without allowing any further hits and felt the euphoria of the final out of the game. Like a diamond under the earth’s surface, Rio thrived under pressure. 

When the game finished, the fans rushed the field in celebration. It was a beautiful moment of chaos. There were still four games on the schedule, but winning the first felt special. 

“Rio, you did it! You really did it!” Her uncle raced over to her immediately, followed by Jen. 

“I’ve never seen you play like that!” Jen yelled to be heard over the noise. 

Agatha was swarmed by her numerous fans, who were eagerly holding out baseballs and cards to try to get her autograph. Peggy looked stunned in the middle of it all as a tall, All-American looking man leaned down to speak to her. Wanda had taken shelter in the dugout with the twins. Dottie was lapping it all up. Eventually the umpires got a handle on things and the announcer helped clear the field of all non-players. 

Coach Grant corralled them back into the locker room as the excitement died down. 

“One down. That was a close one too, but just like always, you gals showed up when you needed to. Let’s keep the train chugging tomorrow!” He kept it short tonight. The entire team was on too much of a high to sit through a long speech. 

“Y’all, we could actually win this.” Dottie stood up on the bench, her cap was on backwards, “I’m so dang proud to be a Comet right now.” The group hollered their approval. 

As the team happily packed up and went out to greet their loved ones, Peggy, Agatha, and Rio were the only ones left. 

Agatha saw Peggy picking at the knots in her mitt. “Rio, I’ll come out soon, okay? Don’t leave until I do.” The pitcher nodded and went. 

“Peg, I saw him.” Agatha sat beside her on the worn wooden bench. 

The beautiful Brit looked up with tears in her eyes, “I thought it was a dream. I’ve imagined it enough times.”

“It was real. How did he find you? Where has he been?” 

Peggy had met Steve Rogers in 1942 in Boston. He was on leave from the war. Agatha remembered the night in the bar when they had first connected. Those two spent a few glorious weeks together before he had to ship off back to the front lines. All she was left with was his silver lighter and the memory. He never got in touch again, and Peggy never got over him. 

“He got injured and was recovering in a hospital in Berlin for several years. He got back to the states this summer and settled down in New York. It was just pure chance he saw an article about us in the Post. My name was mentioned, so he drove all the way here. It’s like something out of a movie!” She laughed at the absurdity. 

“How did he know it was the right Peggy Carter?” Agatha asked. 

“He just hoped it was! He’s waiting for me outside. He asked to take me out - said I owed him one more dance.” Peggy’s voice trembled. She was normally so sure of herself, so confident with men. 

“Why’re you hiding in here then?”

“It’s been so long. I moved on. I tried so hard to move on. What if he doesn’t want me anymore? I’ve not exactly been a saint while he was away.” 

“You’ll never find out in this dingy locker room. That man drove across four states on the off chance that he could see you again. Give him a chance at least.” Agatha stood up and offered her hand to help Peggy stand too. 

“You’re right.” Peggy dusted off her dress. “Keep the window cracked for me tonight?”

“Always.” Agatha walked with her out of the hallway towards the exit. Steve was standing against the telephone booth, as handsome as ever. Peggy gave Agatha one last look before rushing off into his waiting arms. 

Rio was absorbed in conversation with her guests when Agatha walked over. 

“Oh, here’s someone I wanted you to meet. Uncle Hector, this is Agatha Harkness, the catcher on the Comets. She’s taught me so much since I joined the team.” Rio explained. 

Hector gave Agatha a firm handshake, “Thank you for helping my girl. You two were so in sync out there. Truly professional.”

“Rio certainly makes my job easy. She’s easily the most talented pitcher I’ve ever caught for.” 

“Natural born talent. That’s what I always said. She was throwing as hard as her cousins when she was barely this tall.” He held a hand up to his waist to indicate height. “I’m glad other people have the chance to see what I’ve always known.”

Rio fought against the tears at the incredibly heartfelt compliment. Jen noticed immediately and tried to redirect the conversation, “Are you resting tomorrow, Rio?”

“Yeah, I’ll be on the bench unless I get called in. Agatha will be playing though.”

“Is the other pitcher as good as our Rio?” Jen asked. 

Agatha pretended to hum and haw over it to rile Rio up before giving a diplomatic response, “They’re all good in different ways. Lupe has more experience - she’s very talented.” 

Jen responded, “If you say so. Hey, we were going to go get some late night grub. Did you want to join?”

Agatha saw a very subtle shake of the head from Rio, “I’ve got other plans, but thank you for the invite. It was a pleasure to meet you, Hector, and you again Jen. I’ll see you tomorrow hopefully.” 

Instead, she went straight back home to Gertie and Pearl’s. They had already retired to their rooms, so Agatha took a quick shower and went to bed as well. She laid on top of the blankets due to the heat and stared at the popcorn ceiling. 

She replayed the moment with Wanda in the dugout. The redhead had approached her with such vitriol and fear. Agatha knew she was trying to protect her children, but protect them from what? They were friends. They had been friends anyway. It was all gone. Their entire history erased just like that. 

Just because she had fallen for Rio? How could that change the entire foundation of their friendship? It seemed so petty and small. Why couldn’t Wanda let it go? But then, Agatha felt like she couldn’t let it go either. 

Her relationship with Rio was like a giant tattoo inked to her chest. It was so deep in her skin, yet at any moment, it felt like someone could pull back her shirt and reveal it to the world. 

It felt rebellious, and this was not an age of rebellion. 

The second game was also at home in Kenosha, and just as many fans packed in to watch their team take on the Peaches. 

Peggy came home around midnight. Agatha heard her stumble and trip over a loose house slipper after climbing in the window. 

“Peggy?” She mumbled in her sleepy state. 

“Go back to sleep. I’m fine.” She reassured her. 

Now on their walk to the stadium, Agatha got all the details, “Was it like you pictured?”

Peggy physically swooned, “Better. He’s the whole package. A real sort.”

“What’s your rating?”

“We didn’t sleep together!” Peggy exclaimed, which stopped Agatha dead in her tracks. 

“No!”

“Yes! We just sat at the bar all night and talked. He told me about his plans for the future, asked me about what I want to do with my life, and what I’ve been up to. We just…talked.”

“That’s so sweet I feel like I’ve got a cavity.” Agatha knew that Peggy wanted to settle down one day 

“Thanks, doll. And what about your happy ending?” She wondered. 

“Rio?”

“No, Gregory Peck.” Peggy sarcastically replied, “Yes, obviously Rio.” 

“I don’t think we’re going to have a happy ending like you.” Agatha kicked a loose pebble on the sidewalk and watched it bounce into the gutter. 

“Why not?”

Agatha sighed heavily, “The world isn’t built for us! Have you noticed how Wanda’s been lately around me?”

“Yeah, what’s her deal?”

“She found out. She saw Rio and I kissing after practice and basically disowned me - said she didn’t want me around the twins.”

Peggy gasped and put her hand over her mouth, “I thought Little Red was just having a bad day. I didn’t realize…god, I should have known. I’m sorry.”

“You have nothing to apologize for. She just said what everyone else would in this situation.” Agatha’s head fell. 

“Not me. It’s close minded. I’ve never seen you happier than when you’re with Rio. Don’t let one fool ruin that.”

“I can’t even focus on that right now. It’s too big. All I want now is to win these next games. This is what we used to dream about before all this lovey dovey nonsense!” Agatha, ever the deflector, turned the conversation around to baseball - safe, not scary baseball. 

Peggy had a glint in her eye but didn’t push too hard, “Life seems so easy on the field - just a game of winners and losers.”

“Let’s make sure we’re the winners.” Agatha picked up her pace as they approached the ballpark. 

Lupe led the team on defence from the pitcher’s mound this time as Rio rested her arm. The Spanish Striker was a veteran hurler at this point, and no stranger to the finals but had never won one. 

Agatha liked the predictability that Lupe brought. It was easier on the mitt and the mind - a welcome break from Rio. The first two innings flew by as the Peaches failed to connect with the ball in any meaningful way. 

In the third, Peggy scored off a long fly ball off Agatha’s bat. Then, as payback Babs Miller, the centerfielder, hit a monster homer to tie up the game 1-1. Lupe took it on the chin, but Agatha could see the frustration building. 

“It’s alright. It’s still early in the game. Let’s keep those bats going. Come on!” Coach Grant counselled them as they entered the fourth inning. 

Things remained all tied up inning after inning. In the seventh, Rockford were up to bat again, and Martha was on first base. Their catcher, Carol, ripped one right past Peggy at shortstop and Martha took off, rounding second, going for third. Shirley scooped up the ball and launched it to Horsey at third, who tagged the runner for a smooth out. The crowd applauded the impressive play by the fielders. 

In the last inning of the game, things were getting desperate. Neither team had scored. The Comets were up first. Dottie entered the box, raring to hit. She swung way too hard at the first pitch and went right over it for a strike. 

“Lay off the low ones!” Peggy called out. 

The next pitch missed the zone, but the following one was a curveball, just outside. Dottie swung and got a piece of it. The ball slid across the dirt towards second base, but the pitcher fielded it quickly and tossed it to first for an out. 

“Bad luck, kid.” Rio offered as Dottie re-entered the dugout slowly. 

Wanda was up next. The redhead had barely spoken to anyone the past two games. She seemed distant and removed. They all figured she was trying to disconnect early since this was her last season. Agatha knew the truth. 

The first pitch was way outside. A clear mistake by the pitcher, Alice Hall. Agatha didn’t know much about her. She used to be an outfielder, but they must have re-trained her as a pitcher when the league went overhand. She lacked finesse and control. 

Wanda gripped the bat tight and swung away at the third pitch.. 

The announcer’s voice howled, “She is red hot tonight! Wanda Maximoff sends one outta here! Homeeeeee runnnnnn!!!”

The team jumped and screamed in the dugout as Wanda touched every base. The Comets were now leading 2-1. 

As the redhead returned, everyone patted her on the back and congratulated her. Agatha went in for a celebratory hug out of excitement, which was instantly extinguished when Wanda cringed away and avoided even touching her. Oh right, I’m the enemy now. 

Peggy noticed and shot daggers at Wanda in protest. Rio was too far away to have seen anything. 

“She’s lucky she’s leaving because otherwise I’d been having serious words with her.” Peggy was fuming as she watched Wanda celebrate with the rest of the teammates. 

“Just leave it. She’s not worth it.” Agatha said. She didn’t want to stir up more drama than necessary this close to the season’s end. 

The game finished with another Comets win. One more and that was it.

One more win and they would be champions. 

Rio was the starter for game three, which would be their last in Kenosha. As the winners of the league, they had secured home field advantage, but if the series went to game four and five, they would have to travel to Rockford. 

“I hope you guys finish them off tonight.” Jen said over breakfast at the diner with Rio and Hector. 

“Yeah me too. I don’t think my arm can make it much longer.” 

“Are you hurting, mija?” Hector asked with concern. 

“I’m fine. It just gets a bit sore after going a full nine innings. And I’m giving it my all, so it’s extra tender. But I’ll be alright.” Rio knew how much her body could take. 

She loved having her family here, but she also missed Agatha deeply. The two hadn’t been able to spend any time alone together. Things had been so hectic that they barely had time to see each other at all outside the games. And time was ticking down fast. 

Rio finally caught Agatha a few minutes before their pre-game practice. 

“Hey, can we talk?” Rio asked, nodding towards the equipment closet. They stepped into the room filled with buckets of baseballs, old mitts and cleats, and racks full of all sorts of broken and old bats. It could maybe fit four people snugly and was lit by a single, small rectangular window on the back wall. 

“What’s up?” Agatha leaned against the shelving and crossed her arms. 

“I miss you.” Rio leaned back against the wall opposite the catcher. There was only an arm’s length between them. 

“Rio…”

“Why don’t you want me?”

“I can’t.”

“Can’t what?” Rio was tired of this hot and cold behavior. “I know Wanda got in your head, but I don’t want to waste what little time we have left. What if this is it?”

“We could see each other next season. Like Greta and Carson.” Agatha offered. 

“I thought you were done. I thought you were retiring.” Rio remembered Agatha mentioning that before. 

“I haven’t decided yet. This won’t be goodbye forever either way. We’ll find a way to see each other.” Agatha wanted to believe that was true. 

“How?”

“What do you mean? I’ll give you my phone number. You can call me anytime. You can come visit if you want. I’m not going to disappear, Rio.”

The pitcher finally released a smile. She took a chance and pushed off the wall and stepped forward into Agatha’s space. She felt the shift in the air as her hands found Agatha’s waist. The walls felt like they were closing in around them. 

Rio paused, her face just an inch or so from Agatha’s. She breathed in the air coming from Agatha’s lungs and enjoyed the radiating heat from the other’s close body. 

Agatha realized Rio was giving her a choice by not going all the way. She could run. Dip out of the closet and get back to the game, forget this dance with the devil. Instead, she chose the second option. She slammed their lips together in a forceful kiss. She bit hard on Rio’s bottom lip and then soothed it with her tongue. She pushed the pitcher backwards until she hit the wall and moaned at the contact. 

It was hello, it was goodbye, it was I don’t know what this is and I can’t even think right now to figure it out. 

When she came up for air, she felt energized, “Go on, get to the locker room before they notice we’re late.” 

“Why do I have to go first?” Rio wondered, still dazed from the kiss. 

“Because I like to watch you.” Agatha grinned. She felt invincible. Maybe, for once, things were going to work out in her favor. 

After the warm up, right before the anthem, Agatha addressed the team, “This could be our last game. We’ve played over a hundred games together this season, and it all comes down to this. We could finish it right here, right now. Some of you know that I joined the league to run from something, to run from my problems back home. I used to do that a lot. Run away from anything that scared me. I still struggle with that.”

She gave Rio a sympathetic nod. A tiny apology that only she would understand. 

Agatha continued, “But I’m trying. This league has taught me how to be brave, how to be strong, how to fight for what I want. And all I want right now is to win! I’ve accomplished so many of my goals so far. Help me cross off this one, and I’ll owe you all my life. Put your hands in.” 

The team piled their hands on top of each other in a circle. 

Agatha led them, “Fight on three. One, two, three.”

“FIGHT!”

Agatha thought back to her previous life, her life before baseball. She had been a wife and a mother. She had been drifting - a passenger in her life. When it all disappeared, she was like a ship with no anchor. Baseball had pulled her back to shore. It had been her lighthouse in a storm. As she took her place behind the plate, she knew this might be the last time. 

It had been five years of highs and lows. The entire game revolved around the 17 inch plate in front of her. The white rubber saw it all - the elation of a walk-off home run, the devastation of a third out strikeout, the relief of a safe slide for a run. 

Agatha had been there for it all. There was only one more thing she wanted to achieve in her career before retiring. 

As the game got underway, every player had the same goal in mind, though different motivations. 

Right Field - Fern “Fossey” Foss

The first inning yielded no action for the right fielder. The Canadian had only played in the league for two years. She prided herself on her strong arm and was training with Rio to learn how to pitch. Rio was the best teacher she’d had. Fossey loved learning something new. 

She’d been recruited after a scout spotted her playing on her town team in the city championship. That had been the last time she’d played in a big game like this. 

Her team lost that day. She wasn’t going to repeat that mistake again. 

Center Field - Loretta “Buckets” Buckley

Loretta caught a pop-up in the second inning for an out and threw it in to hold the runner at first. Buckets, as the team affectionately called her, was 28 and hailed from Knoxville, Tennessee. She’d lied to her mama at first and said she was volunteering to collect war bonds because she would never have been allowed to leave home otherwise. Baseball had been her private hobby. She never imagined that she’d be able to earn a salary from it. 

When the cheques started arriving back home, her mama was so happy for the extra cash that she didn’t bother asking where the money was coming from. Buckets could swing a bat with enough power to clear the fences and had impressive speed on the bases.

In the bottom of the second, she hit a line drive through the gap between third and short and got on base. She stole second but ended up stranded. Buckets hated being left on base. It was like getting a tiny taste of a delicious meal and not being able to finish. She knew how much the rest of the team wanted to win, and she wanted to contribute. 

Left Field - Shirley Cohen

The native New Yorker had baseball running through her blood. Her father and her grandfather had played the sport as boys in the streets of Brooklyn. She had grown up going to Robins (later renamed to the Dodgers) games whenever they were able to scrounge up money for tickets. Shirley loved baseball like some people loved a sibling. She had grown up with it. It was a constant throughout every year. It had brought her joy. It had brought her heartache.

She was a hypochondriac in her regular life, but on the field, she was rough and tumble. She would dive and slide and put her body on the line to make a play. All her anxiety faded away when a mitt was on her hand. Her father told her not to bother coming home until she won a trophy, so she lived in Chicago during the off-season. 

In the third inning, she saw a juicy curveball approaching the plate while she was up. She remembered hearing Johnny Frederick, the Robins outfielder, once on the radio saying that hitting is all about timing. She laid back and let the ball approach. She used her hips to swing the bat around and smacked it hard. The ball followed the first base foul line and landed just fair. 

“Go Shirley!” She heard the crowd scream as she rounded the bags. Coach Grant motioned towards him frantically, calling her to third. She booked it and watched him as he pointed down. She slid. 

“Safe!” 

Shirley jumped up and felt like the winning show pony. She’d just hit a triple. 

Third Base - Rose “Horsey” Horstman

The hometown girl, Horsey, hooted and hollered as Shirley sped around the bases. Rose was born and raised in Kenosha. Her parents had settled down in this suburb after fleeing the chill of Minneapolis. She liked the small town feeling and the community spirit. When Mr. Wrigley decided to base one of the new women’s ballclubs here, it felt like destiny. 

Horsey had three older sisters and always felt like the black sheep. While they were all preoccupied with dolls, make-up, and the neighborhood boys, Horsey would trail after their father to his recreational baseball games. She learned how to catch by playing outfield during their batting practices and how to accurately spit chewing tobacco at way too young an age. 

Her father always lamented never making the majors. He had reached the minors as a young man, but when his future wife got pregnant, he gave up the game and took a carpentry apprenticeship instead. He may have left the game, but it never left him. 

When Horsey came home with a contract to play pro ball, he cried for the first time in decades. 

After Shirley hit the triple, Buckets batted her in with a dangerous grounder that took a nasty hop and bounced right past the Peaches second baseman. They were first on the scoreboard. 

“That’s it! Way to go, Comets!!” Horsey could hear her father’s voice above the crowd. His midwest accent and distinctive low tone was recognizable to her anywhere. He came to every home game and sat right behind their dugout. He would probably die of happiness if they won tonight. 

She felt like she owed this to him.

Shortstop - Peggy Carter

In the top of the fourth inning, a ball off Martha Everett came right off the bat towards Peggy. She saw its trajectory and nabbed it in her mitt, tossed the ball to Wanda at second for the force out, then on to Dottie at first for a double play. 

She looked to the stands and saw Steve on his feet, clapping loudly, and her heart soared. She couldn’t believe that he was really here. She had given up hope so long ago and filled her heart with beautiful distractions.

Baseball had long since failed to excite her. She mostly stayed for Agatha and the steady pay. It was a great escape from daily life. 

But lately, all she daydreamed about was daily life. She found her mind drifting to a house in the suburbs, a handful of children, and slow dancing in the living room with a man she loved. She never wanted to admit that the man she imagined bore a striking resemblance to the military officer who stole her heart six years ago. However, now that he was real and just steps away in the stands, she could see it as a possibility. 

As the inning turned over, she was up to bat. Dottie was on first. One out. The ball came in low and slow for a ball. The next two were outside the zone as well. Three balls, no strikes. The pitcher looked worried. The last pitch was high. She took the walk - a free pass to first base. 

Shirley popped one up high next. The umpire called an infield fly, thus the batter was out. Agatha stepped up. Two outs. Two runners on base. Peggy saw the fire in her friend’s eyes. She was so focussed. 

Peggy hoped that if they won this game, they could finally retire. She could finally start a brand new life. 

Agatha clobbered the ball. Peggy watched it, holding her run until the ball dropped. It looked like it had a chance but instead hit the dirt inside the fence. Peggy saw Dottie booking it home, touching home for another run. The fans were going wild. She kept an eye on the ball as it hit the cut-off. She could make it home. She forced her legs to move as she felt the burn in her thighs. She touched home plate as the ball flew wide and missed the catcher. 

Comets 3, Peaches 0. 

Peggy looked up to the bleachers. Steve was waving to get her attention. His eyes seemed to reflect the bright lights - they were glowing at her. He raised his hand and blew her a kiss. It was so innocent and stupidly romantic. Peggy caught it in her dusty hand and felt the goosebumps break out across her arms. 

Trophy or not, she felt like she’d already won. 

Second base - Wanda “Little Red” Maximoff

Going into the fifth inning, they had a healthy lead. Wanda carried the worry on her shoulders but felt it ease a little bit. This was her last season. There were no re-dos, no second chances. She had decided at the start of the year that this was it. 

She was so ready to leave this league behind. She was grateful for the experience and the salary, but the past few weeks had tainted her memory of it all. Wanda did not want her sons around people like this. They were about to start school. She wanted them to have stability, normalcy, and a regular life. 

She’d saved a good chunk of her pay from the league, but the bonus from winning the championship would be a welcome goodbye gift. She would use it to buy new furniture for the boys’ room. They deserved the very best, and she’d do whatever it took to give it to them. 

Babs Miller lined one right at her. Wanda jumped high and was able to catch it in the air for an out. The Peaches were struggling to put the ball in play. They had a few hits but no runs. Rio was so good at giving them nothing good to hit. Wanda didn’t understand how Rio and Agatha could…no, she didn’t want to think about that further. 

She just wanted to win this game and get out of here. 

First base - Dorothy “Dottie” Simpson

The next Peaches batter was Mary Richards. Dottie knew her well. They used to play together in the same county softball league back home in South Carolina. Mary stole the most bases of any player in league history. She had been recruited from the track team and proved her worth immediately.

Dottie was the opposite. Tall, lanky, and slow. She excelled as a first baseman, mostly due to being a lefty. 

Her parents thought she was joking when she said she was moving to Wisconsin to play baseball. The youngest of five, she was the clown of the bunch, but when she showed them the contract, they realized their jokester was serious. 

Dottie promised her mother she’d still go to church every Sunday (she didn’t) and that she’d never touch alcohol (she did), and they let her go. 

The charming 24-year-old had never been away from home in her life, and she loved every second of it. There were none of the old Southern conventions and expectations on her. She could earn her own money, live away from her parents, and skip church. She never wanted this career to end. She hoped to play ball for the rest of her life. They would have to drag her from the field kicking and screaming before she would give up this freedom. 

Mary hit a grounder to third. Horsey threw it hard across the infield to Dottie, but Mary was too fast - safe. 

“Evening, Dottie.” Mary drawled out as she kept one foot on first base. 

“How ya doin’?” Dottie smiled at her old acquaintance. 

The next batter got set. Mary took a lead off the base. Dottie remained close to tag her out if needed. Agatha was closely watching the runner. Mary took another small step towards second. Agatha gave a signal and Rio threw it to first. Dottie tagged Mary but was too late - she’d already stepped back on the base. 

“So close, but yet…” Mary murmured. Dottie bit her tongue. Her mother always said if you have nothing nice to say, don’t say nothing at all. 

Rio struck out the batter for the second out. 

“Looks like y’all just can’t get it together tonight.” Dottie took the turn to gloat this time as she circled the base. Mary sucked her teeth and stayed quiet. 

The Peaches catcher, Carol, was up. On the very first pitch, Mary took off. Dottie yelled out “Steal!” and saw Agatha pop up, catch the ball, and fire to second. It was a millisecond too late. Mary was safe. The runner saluted Dottie, which only made her angrier. 

Luckily, Rio squashed any hope of scoring by striking out Carol and ending the inning. Dottie jogged past Mary as they crossed paths, “Better luck next time.” She grinned. 

The Peaches seemed off their game. Dottie felt like nothing could stop the Comets now.

Winning the championship would put her in a much stronger position for contract negotiations next year. She could ask for a raise finally (even though she would do this job for free).

Coach - Victor “Doc” Grant

Four innings to go. This was the closest he had ever been to a win. He had made it to the Minor League World Series with the Chattanooga Lookouts when he was 22, but they lost it in game six. When he played for the Reds, they never even made it to the post-season. Then, his knee went and that was that. 

Doc was single. He’d been engaged once upon a time to Sally Knight, one of his old teammate’s sisters. When they were planning the wedding, he got the call that he’d been selected as one of the coaches for the All-American Girls Professional Baseball League. He could either stay in Ohio and pick out his wedding tux, or pack up his life and move to Wisconsin.

He had his bags packed that night. 

Now it was all about to pay off. If he could secure this win and lead the Comets to victory, he might get an offer from a minor league team or even an assistant position in the majors. He had seen it happen for others, why not him?

“Keep pushing, Rio! You got this!” He encouraged the pitcher. She was a phenomenon. He wondered whether any male baseball teams would give her a chance. He felt confident that she could handle it. 

Rio kept the Peaches score at zero as they entered the bottom of the fifth. 

Chaperone - Lilia Calderu

There wasn’t much for a chaperone to do during the games. She would occasionally patch up cuts and injuries, especially from slides. Most of the time, Lilia spent the time observing the night sky. On this September evening, there was a half moon shining over them. 

She knew that tonight was the conjunction of the Moon and Jupiter, which often signified financial gains. During this time, people often felt healthy and ambitious. It was the perfect omen for this game. The team appeared to be in high spirits, which could be due to Saturn’s opposition with the sun. 

Lilia enjoyed the atmosphere of excitement around her even as she felt separate from it all. She considered going back to nursing sometimes, but other times, she doubted she could handle the stress again. This unexpected career was a nice way to stay connected with the community in her old age. 

Retirement sounded like a drip. She didn’t know how long this would last, but she was going to enjoy it while she could. 

Catcher - Agatha “Angel” Harkness

The game was going better than expected. Agatha watched Fossey step up to bat. She hit a fly ball towards left, but the third baseman was able to track back and catch it. Buckets was up next. She fouled two and then swung at a tricky cutter - two outs. 

“Save us, Rio, you’re our only hope.” Agatha cupped her hands and shouted towards the pitcher who was taking a turn in the lineup. 

Rio stood tall and waited on it. She watched two strikes pass her by. Agatha could tell that she recognized them, but Rio was patient, she was waiting for something. A ball flew wide, then the pitcher gave Rio just what she wanted - fastball, outside corner. 

“There she goes! The Reaper sends it back, back, oh no! It’s foul! Foul ball!” The announcer yelled in disappointment as the ball hooked left and landed in the stands foul. Agatha watched Rio’s face fall as she was forced back into the batter’s box to try again. The next pitch was a changeup, but Rio anticipated speed and swung too early. Strike out. 

As the pitcher trudged back into the dugout, Agatha remarked, “Never thought I’d see the day.”

“Don’t test me.” Rio snapped, still angry from her plate appearance. 

“Just kidding! We’re way ahead, you’ve got nothing to worry about.” Agatha said. 

Back in the field in the sixth inning, Rio was back to her normal self. Her arm was like a cannon. She kept reloading and firing at full capacity as if she had endless powder in the tank. Hattie Walker was up and jittery as there were already two outs. Agatha called for a knuckleball, which worked like a charm for strike one. 

The next pitch, she gave the sign for a fastball. Hattie swung and the ball shot straight up in the air. Agatha ripped her mask off and looked up. The ball was arcing right fast. She sprinted towards the fence, never taking her eye off the ball as it fell towards the stands. Agatha didn’t hesitate, she jumped and reached for the ball as her body careened over the barrier and into the fans in the front row. 

She never let her arm drop. Her glove was high in the air, grasping the baseball firmly. She’d caught it! Her head was in someone’s lap, her legs were askew, but she had caught it. Another inning retired. 

“What a play by Angel Harkness! You’ll never see a better catch than that! That was incredible!” She could hear the announcer’s voice over the cheers. 

One of the fans helped push her up, she stood on her feet, and she felt it. 

No. 

No. 

No. 

Her knee buckled. She tried to step over the low fence to get back on the field, and her right leg wouldn’t bend. 

Fuck. Fuck. No, no!

She tried to put pressure on it and almost screamed in agony. She couldn’t bend it, she couldn’t put weight on it. She tottered on one leg and panicked. 

“Agatha? What’s wrong?” Rio had immediately run over to help her. 

“My knee.” Agatha’s voice broke. Rio sat on the wall and helped Agatha do the same. She helped her swing her legs around to the field side and then lifted her over to the dirt. Agatha tried to stand again and would have collapsed if Rio’s arm hadn’t been around her waist. 

“ Agatha… ” Rio began. 

“No!” Agatha cried out. She could barely recognize her own voice. All she knew was that this couldn’t be it. She couldn’t end her career like this. She tried again to put weight on her leg as Rio practically carried her to the dugout. The pain was blinding, but she forced it down and was able to take a step. Then another, then another. 

“How did you catch that ball, Angel? I’ve never seen anything like that before!” Horsey asked as they hobbled to the bench. Rio eased her down on the bench, and she lifted her leg to rest on it. 

“Alright, Harkness?” Coach Grant stood before her. He wasn’t blind. He knew that look all too well. The fear on every athlete’s face when their body fails them. 

“Just peachy.” Agatha declared with her signature smile, trying to hide the pain. “Ha, get it?”

The coach's eyes narrowed, “Stand up.”

“I’m tired, sir. Can’t a girl have a rest?” 

“Agatha. If you don’t stand, I’m pulling you.”

The catcher chewed the insult she wanted to dish out. She set her jaw and bit the inside of her cheek as she lowered her leg and pushed off the bench. It was torture, but she knew how to handle pain. 

They weren’t going to take this away from her. 

She stood unsteadily and stared at the coach with a look that said see?

She did what he had asked. She wasn’t going to let him bench her. She deserved to play. She deserved to win. 

For once in her life, she deserved to come out on top. 

Pitcher - Rio “The Reaper” Vidal

Agatha was not okay in any sense of the word. Rio’s heart was shattering watching her act like nothing was wrong. She was so desperate to win that she was willing to give up her body to get it.

“I can see you’re going to be stubborn about this, Harkness. So it’s not up to you anymore. Rio, you tell me what I should do. You need a catcher who can actually catch.”

Rio’s world stopped. 

She didn’t want to do this. She couldn’t be the one to decide…this. 

Agatha stared at her with a pleading sorrow in her eyes, “Please.” Then Rio swore she mouthed the words “My love” but she couldn’t be sure. Her vision felt blurred and hazy. 

Rio replayed every moment together. The fights, the laughs, the unbelievable love. How was it all coming down to this?

She knew Agatha wanted to win. She couldn’t imagine winning without her. But, she couldn’t see how Agatha could play the rest of the game. She might do serious damage to her knee and end up permanently injured - and for what? Was a trophy worth a lifetime of pain? 

Rio closed her eyes as Agatha’s pleas got louder, “Please, Rio. Please! I need more time. Please!”

The dugout was silent as the team watched on helplessly. Tears fell quietly. Nobody wanted to see a fellow player get benched for an injury. 

Rio opened her eyes and met Agatha’s. They were pulsing with agony as if she was trying to hypnotize Rio into letting her stay. Her hair was matted with sweat, her hands were shaking. Rio wished she could tear off her own leg and offer it up as sacrifice. 

“If you do this, I will hate you forever.” Agatha’s words sliced through her. The pain felt like a relief from the incoming guilt. 

Rio looked at Coach Grant. If she could prevent Agatha from an awful injury, she could live with the grief of this betrayal. The whole team was counting on this win. She needed this to be over. She needed this to be done. 

She hardened her heart and delivered the final blow, “She can’t play.”

Agatha descended into sobs. Her face distorted with pain as her injury and the words crushed her. Peggy grabbed her before she fell to the ground and escorted her out of the dugout as the team could only watch in shock. 

Rio wouldn’t see Agatha again…

for over fifteen years.

Chapter End Notes

I've had this planned for a while now, and it still hurt to write.

End game is always Agathario though - do not fret.

Chapter 19: Holding the runner

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“Then came the news that there was to be no more professional girls baseball. It was like a death in the family for me.”

Sarah Jane Sands

 

March 1963

Cambridge, Massachusetts 

The lecture hall emptied with a stampede after the professor released the class for the morning. Each student rushing on to their next class or their next break.

“William.”

The young man paused on the steps as Professor Emerson called out his name. 

“Sir?”

“You live near Cambridge Common, right?”

“Yes.”

“Are you able to deliver this to Dr. Goodwin in the medical department at Radcliffe College? I would normally ask my assistant but he’s off sick today.” The professor handed over a heavy textbook and a folder of papers. 

“Not a problem, sir. I’ll head straight there.” William shouldered his bag and held the delivery close as he rushed up the stairs and out of the building. 

It was spring on campus - the snow had finally dissipated and the flowers were peeking out from their hibernation. Harvard was picture perfect. William was 20 years old and finishing up his sophomore year. He finally felt settled in, as his first year had felt like being dropped into an ice cold lake. Walking around campus now, it felt familiar and comfortable. 

“Hey there.” Eddie appeared from nowhere, suddenly walking in lockstep with him. 

“Hey!” William gave him a genuine smile. Eddie lived across the hall and was…well, they hadn’t decided what they were yet. 

“I thought you had a break now?”

“Yeah, I’ve just got to deliver something to a professor at the women’s college.” 

“Alright, I’ll meet you back at my dorm.” Eddie showed off his adorable dimple and leaned close, “I’ll keep the bed warm.”

William felt his face flush, and he nodded quietly, while speed walking to get this errand over with. He had never visited the Radcliffe buildings before. It was Harvard’s sister school for women as the Ivy League institution was still male-only.

They shared the same faculty as Harvard, so the students were taught by some of the greatest minds in their respective fields. 

He found the medical building easily. The four story brick building was in classical colonial style like much of the campus. He walked in the large wooden doors and scanned the directions on the wall. Room 235 - Medical Research. 

The stairs were to his left. It was just after 10AM, and students were coming and going down the hallways. As he approached room 235, groups of women were exiting. He waited outside the door to get in. 

There were all sorts of women coming out of the room. Most looked older than him - it must be a graduate level course. His eyes connected with one woman, who was by herself. He did a double then triple take as she passed. Why did she look so familiar? 

William trawled his mind. He knew that face. He couldn’t place where. She was halfway down the hall. It couldn’t be…could it? 

“Rio?” He ran, calling out the name he couldn’t believe he pulled from his memory.

His dress shoes pounded the tiles. She turned. 

Her hair was much shorter than he remembered and cut in a stylish swooping bob. She was dressed in a dark skirt with a matching vest over a white shirt. But he would remember that face anywhere.

His mom kept a team photograph hidden in the office drawers. Growing up, he and his twin used to sneak looks at it when she was busy. It was a reminder of the years they spent on the road with the women’s professional baseball league. A reminder that it had really happened - no matter how his mom tried to pretend it didn’t. 

“I’m sorry, do I know you?” She asked as she eyed him up and down. 

“I’m William Maximoff.” He readjusted the book to one arm and extended his right hand. He saw a flicker of recognition. 

“Maximoff?” She shook his hand gently. 

“I used to go by Billy. You played ball with my mother, Wanda.” 

Rio blinked rapidly, and her skin seemed to pale as she squinted at him hard, “You were the twin?”

“Yes!! My brother Tommy! I knew it was you!” William had a distinct memory of watching Rio warm up before every game. She had such a unique pitching style. 

“Wow, I haven’t thought about the league in…years.” Rio stared off into the distance.

“Yeah, my mom doesn’t like to talk about it either. I don’t know why. Those are some of my best childhood memories!”

“I can’t believe you remember me.” 

“You’re pretty memorable. Can you wait just a sec? I need to drop off this delivery to the teacher in there. I’ll be right back.” He zipped into the lecture hall and handed over the book and papers to the professor who was packing up, then hustled back out, afraid that Rio might have left. 

She was waiting outside the class, fiddling with the strap of her cross body bag. 

“Are you busy? Do you want to get a coffee with me?” He asked. He was so eager to see someone from his past. It was like this forbidden secret in his house. He wanted to connect with those forgotten years in some way. Eddie would forgive him. 

Rio shrugged her shoulders, “I’ve got another class at one o’clock, but I can spare some time.” 

“Great, want to go to The Unicorn?”

“Lead the way.”

They got a table in the back of the campus cafe. Rio ordered coffee and Billy got an espresso. She settled against the brick, “So how’d you end up at Harvard, kid?”

“I was top of the class in my high school and got accepted. It's been nice to be on my own - away from Tommy. I’m studying Comparative Literature.”

“Literature? What are your plans after you graduate?”

“My dad named me after William Shakespeare, and I fell in love with his plays. I try to read everything I can get my hands on. I want to write my own book one day.” William had the starry-eyed optimism that only exists in the youth. 

Rio smiled, “Impressive. You’re so grown up.”

“Thanks, well what about you? Are you a student or…?

“PhD student.”

“Wow!”

“My job offered to pay for my doctorate, so I jumped at the chance. Radcliffe has one the premier programs in biochemistry. I never thought I’d get in, but here I am. I have one more year to go.” Rio took a long drink. 

“What do you do exactly?” William sipped from his tiny cup and pretended he liked it.
